الاتیان بمثلہ ہونا اعجاز کے منافی نہیں ہے ۔ وعن الثانی خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ اعجاز خواہ طرف اعلیٰ کا ہو یا اس کے قریبی مرتبہ کا یہ دونوں متحد اور ایک ہیں بایں حیثیت کہ کلام کی یہ ایک حد ہے جو بلغ من جميع ما عداہ ہے جس کا معارضہ اور اس
…should be performed in a manner that is more eloquent and more effective than all other methods of communication. The commentator said regarding this: 'It is not an interpretation of the concept of linguistic inimitability.' That is, this is not an explanation of the meaning of i'jaz al-kalam, because i'jaz does not necessarily require eloquence. Rather, i'jaz fi al-kalam is defined as speech reaching a level where it cannot be contested and producing its like is beyond human capacity. It is derived from 'a'jaztuhu' meaning 'I rendered him incapable.' Now it is not necessary that the cause of this i'jaz be eloquence; rather, various factors can be the cause. For this reason, different reasons are given for the Quran being miraculous, despite agreement that it is miraculous. Some say it is due to its eloquence – that the Quran is miraculous because it is at a high level of eloquence beyond human reach. Some say it is due to its reports – because it contains news of the unseen, and humans cannot produce such news. This view is rejected because any surah that does not contain news of the unseen would not be miraculous, but that is incorrect; rather, every surah, even the length of a surah, is miraculous even if it does not contain news of the unseen. Some say it is due to its unique style – its style is different from the prose and poetry of the eloquent. Some say it is by Allah diverting the intellects of the opponents from contesting it. This view is also rejected because it would imply that a completely ineloquent speech could be more miraculous if contestation is merely prevented. Rather, the author's intent is to present the correct view: that the i'jaz of the Quran is based on the fact that its method of conveying meaning is more eloquent than all other methods, and its i'jaz is due to eloquence. Therefore, since i'jaz in speech requires that it be more eloquent than all other methods, that method can only be one, not multiple. Hence the term 'urwat al-i'jaz uses the singular 'urwa, unlike sihr al-kalam which uses the plural 'ahdab al-sihr. 'Urwa is stronger than hadab. The purpose is to make speech subtle and express meanings with appropriate expressions until it approaches sihr and i'jaz. Here there are two investigations: the first concerns the author's statement 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu', and the second concerns his statement 'wa la yakun hadha illa wahidan'. The summary of the first: In the definition of i'jaz as 'conveying meaning through a method more eloquent than all other methods,' what is meant by 'all other methods'? If only actual existing methods, that is insufficient for proving i'jaz, because i'jaz requires impossibility of contestation, and superiority over existing methods does not guarantee that no potential method could contest it. If it means all methods actual and potential, then being more eloquent than all is not a condition for i'jaz, because Allah is able to produce the like of the Quran, so there must be some potential method to produce its like, yet the Quran is unanimously miraculous. So what is the meaning of 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu'? The second investigation: The method of i'jaz is not singular; rather, there are multiple methods because the highest level and what is close to it are both miraculous, as mentioned in Nihayat al-I'jaz. So what is the meaning of 'la yakun illa wahidan'? The answer to the first: The second alternative is chosen – i'jaz requires being more eloquent than all actual and potential methods. Since i'jaz is only in the speech of Allah, the meaning is that compared to all methods possible in the speech of others (actual or potential), it is more eloquent, such that others cannot produce its like. Allah's ability to produce its like does not negate i'jaz. The answer to the second: I'jaz, whether at the highest level or close to it, are unified in that they represent a single limit of speech that is more eloquent than all other methods, which cannot be contested.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that expands upon the definition of i'jaz (inimitability) of the Quran as presented in the original text. The commentator first clarifies that i'jaz fundamentally means rendering others incapable of producing something similar, not necessarily through eloquence alone. He then reviews various scholarly opinions on the cause of the Quran's i'jaz: eloquence, reports of the unseen, unique style, and divine prevention (sarf). He refutes the latter two, affirming that the correct view, according to the author, is that i'jaz is due to superlative eloquence in conveying meanings. The commentator then addresses two investigations raised by this definition. The first concerns the phrase 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu' (more eloquent than all other methods): whether it refers only to actual methods or includes potential ones. He resolves that the intended meaning includes both actual and potential, but this condition is specific to the Quran as the speech of Allah, so the challenge remains. The second investigation questions why the method of i'jaz is described as singular. The commentator explains that i'jaz encompasses both the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it, but these are considered a single limit, hence the singular 'urwa. Throughout, the commentary demonstrates rigorous textual analysis consistent with Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology.

Key Terms
اعجاز (i'jaz): کلام کا اس مرتبہ پر پہنچنا کہ اس کا معارضہ ممکن نہ ہو اور اس کی مثل پیش کرنا طاقت بشر سے خارج ہو جائے (speech reaching a level where it cannot be contested and its like is beyond human capacity)
سحر (sihr): دقت کلام اور ماخذ کے لطیف ہونے کو کہتے ہیں (subtlety of speech and fineness of origin)
عروة (urwa): کڑا یا دستہ جس سے پکڑا جاتا ہے (handle or loop used for holding); metaphor for the singular method of i'jaz

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about i'jaz?
A) It necessarily requires eloquence.
B) It is defined as speech that cannot be contested and is beyond human capacity.
C) It is identical to sihr.
D) It has multiple methods.

Key Takeaway
I'jaz is the property of speech that renders humans incapable of producing its like; in the Quran it is accepted as due to its superlative eloquence.

The Cause of I'jaz: Eloquence vs. Other Views
Scholarly debate on the cause of Quranic inimitability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that i'jaz is due to eloquence and refute the views of reports of unseen, unique style, and divine prevention using arguments from the commentary.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that the Quran's inimitability is due to its superlative eloquence, not any other factor.

This lesson examines the scholarly debate on the cause of the Quran's i'jaz. While all agree the Quran is miraculous, they differ on why. The commentator reviews four views and defends the eloquence position, refuting alternatives with logical arguments. You will learn the Hanafi proof and understand why the other views are rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four views on the cause of i'jaz
List: (1) eloquence, (2) reports of unseen, (3) unique style, (4) divine prevention (sarf). Recognize which is the Hanafi accepted view.
All views acknowledge i'jaz but differ on its source.
2
Analyze the refutation of the second view (reports of unseen)
The commentator argues that some surahs without unseen reports remain miraculous, so this cannot be the sole cause.
This refutation uses counterexample.
3
Analyze the refutation of the third view (unique style)
Unique style alone does not negate i'jaz; the Quran's style is miraculous, but i'jaz is not limited to style.
The argument: style is a characteristic, not necessarily the cause.
4
Analyze the refutation of the fourth view (sarf)
If sarf were true, weaker speech would be more miraculous because it would be harder to contest. This is absurd.
This refutation uses a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Determine the Hanafi tarjih
The commentator states that the author's intent is the correct view: i'jaz is due to eloquence. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih based on definition and consistency.

طریقہ پر ادا کیا جائے جو تمام طرق ادا سے ابلغ اور زیادہ بلیغ ہو شارح نے اس کے متعلق کہا لیس تفسیر المفهوم العجاز الكلام یعنی یہ اعجاز کلامی کے مفہوم کی تفسیر نہیں ہے کیونکہ اعجاز کے اندر یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ وہ بلاغت کے ساتھ ہو بلکہ اعجاز فی الکلام اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ کلام ایسے مرتبہ پر پہنچ جائے کہ اس کا معارضہ کرنا ممکن نہ ہو اور اس کی مثل پیش کرنا طاقت بشر سے خارج ہو جائے یہ اعجزتہ سے ماخوذ ہے جس کا معنی ہے عاجز کر دیتا اب یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ اس اعجاز کا سبب بلاغت ہو بلکہ مختلف امور سبب اعجاز ہو سکتے ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ قرآن مجید کے معجز ہونے میں مختلف وجوہ پیش کئے جاتے ہیں باوجود اس کے کہ معجز ہونے پر اتفاق ہے ۔ فقیل انه ببلاغته یعنی قرآن مجید کا معجز ہونا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ وہ بلاغت کے اونچے مقام پر ہے جہاں قوت انسانی کا پہنچنا ناممکن ہے۔ وقیل باخبارہ یعنی بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ چونکہ قرآن مجید اخبار عن المغیبات پر مشتمل ہے اس لئے معجز ہے کیونکہ انسان اخبار عن المغیبات کی طاقت نہیں رکھتا یہ اس کی حدود علمی سے بالکل خارج ہے۔ اس وجہ کو رد کر دیا گیا ہے کہ جو سورۃ اخبار عن المغیبات پر مشتمل نہ ہو وہ معجز نہ ہو حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے بلکہ ہر سورۃ بلکہ مقدار سورۃ معجز ہے اگر چہ اخبار عن المغیبات پر مشتمل نہ ہو وقیل باسلوبه الغریب یعنی اس کا اسلوب غریب عجیب سے فصحار و بلغار کے اسلوب نثر و نظم دونوں سے مختلف ہے اور اس اسلوب قرآنی سے وہ لوگ نا آشنا تھے وقیل بصورت اللہ تعالیٰ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان معارضین کے عقول کو اپنی قوۃ قاہرہ کے ساتھ اس کے معارضہ سے اور اس کے مثل لانے سے پھیر دیا اور دوسری طرف موڑ دیا اس کے معارضہ کی طرف بالکل آنے نہیں دیا یہ وجہ بھی مردود ہے کیونکہ اس سے یہ لازم آتا ہے جو کلام بلاغت کے بالکل نچلے درجہ میں ہو اور معارضہ سے صرف عقول کر دیا جائے تو اس کا اعجاز قوی تر ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ با وجود ممکن المعارضہ ہونے کے اس کا معارضہ نہ ہو سکے یہ صرف العقول میں اظہر ہے اور اعجاز میں اقوئی ہونی چاہیئے ۔ بل المراد یعنی مصنف کی مراد قرآن مجید کے اعجاز کے متعلق جو صحیح رہی ہے اس کو پیش کرنا ہے یعنی قرآن مجید کا اعجاز صحیح رای کے لحاظ سے اس پر مبنی ہے کہ ادائے معنی کا طریقہ تمام طرق اداء سے ابلغ ہے اور اس کا اعجاز بسبب بلاغت کے ہے ۔ فباعتبار انه چونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام میں شرط ہے کہ وہ اپنے جمیع ما عدا طرق سے ابلغ ہو اس لئے وه طریق واحد ہو سکتا ہے جس میں تعدد نہیں ہوتا اس لئے عروۃ الاعجاز میں لفظ عروہ واحد اختیار کیا بخلاف سحر الکلام کے کہ وہ دقت کلام اور ماخذ کے لطیف ہونے کو کہتے ہیں لہذا اس کے طرق متعددہ اور مراتب مختلفہ ہو سکتے ہیں اس لئے اہداب السحر بلفظ الجمع کہا ہرب ثوب ان پھندنوں وغیرہ کو کہا جاتا ہے جو اطراف ثوب پر ہوتے ہیں اور عروۃ الکوز اس کڑے اور دستے کو کہا جاتا ہے جس سے پکڑا جاتا ہے اویہ بنسبت ہرب کے اقوی ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو اعجاز کے ساتھ مختص کیا جو سحر سے اوثق ہوتا ہے ان کے ساتھ تمسک کرنے سے مراد کلام کو لطیف کرنے اور معانی کو عبارات لائقہ سے ادا کرنے میں مبالغہ کہ نامراد ہے یہاں تک کہ قریب الی السحر والاعجاز ہو جائے وههنا بحثان بحث اول کا تعلق مصنف کے قول ابلغ من جمیع ما عداہ کے ساتھ ہے اور بحث ثانی کا تعلق اس کے قول و لا یکون ہذا الا واحدا کے ساتھ ہے بحث اول کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اعجاز کی تفسیر میں جو یہ کہا گیا ہے کہ ان یودی المعنى بطريق هوا بلغ من جميع ما عداه من الطرق ۔ اس ما عداه من الطرق سے کیا مراد ہے اگر صرف طرق محققہ اور موجودہ مراد ہیں تو یہ اثبات اعجاز میں کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ اعجاز کے اندر ضروری ہے کہ اس کا معارضہ نا ممکن ہو اور اس کی مثل لانے سے عجز ہو اور یہ طرق محققہ موجودہ سے ابلغ ہو جانے کے ساتھ ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ طرق مقدرہ میں کوئی ایسا طریقہ ہو جس کو اختیار کر کے معارضہ کیا جاسکے اور اس کی مثل لائی جا سکے تو اعجاز ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر ما عداه من الطرق سے مراد عام ہو خواہ طرق محققہ ہوں یا مقدرہ ان جمیع سے ابلغ ہو حتیٰ کہ اس کی مثل پیش کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو یہ اعجاز میں شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالی مثل القرآن لانے پر قادر ہے تو اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ طرق مقدرہ میں کوئی ایسا طریقہ ضرور ہے جس سے مثل قرآن حاصل ہو سکتی ہے حالانکہ قرآن مجید اس احتمال کے باوجود بالاتفاق معجز ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمیع طرق محققہ و مقدرہ سے ابلغ ہونا اعجازہ میں شرط نہیں ہے فما معنی قولہ ابلغ من جميع ما عداه - والثانی اس بحث ثانی کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعجاز کا طریق صرف واحد نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے بھی متعدد طرق ہیں کیونکہ طرف اعلیٰ اور ما يقرب منہ یعنی مراتب گلیہ میں سے جو طرف اعلیٰ کے قریب ہے جس کا معارضہ اور اس کی مثل لانا بشر کے لئے ممکن نہیں یہ دونوں معجز ہیں جیسے مفتاح سکا کی اور شیخ کی نہایۃ الاعجاز میں مذکور ہے تو اس وقت طرق اعجاز بھی متعدد ہوئے بعض طرف اعلیٰ پر اور بعض اس مرتبہ پر جو قریب من الاعلیٰ ہے فما معنی قولہ لا یکون بنا الا واحدا ۔ والجواب عن الاول جواب کے اندرشق ثانی اختیار کی گئی ہے یعنی اعجاز کے اندرا بلغ من جمیع ما عداه من الطرق المحققة والمقدرة کلیتہا شرط ہے پھر چونکہ اعجاز صرف کلام اللہ میں ہے لہذا مرا من الالعجی یہ ہوگی کہ کلام غیر اللہ تعالیٰ میں جتنے طرق ادا ہو سکتے ہیں خواہ محقق ہوں یا مقدر ان تمام سے ابلغ ہو حتیٰ کہ غیر اللہ کے لئے اس کی مثل پیش کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو اب اللہ تعالیٰ کا قادر علی الاتیان بمثلہ ہونا اعجاز کے منافی نہیں ہے ۔ وعن الثانی خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ اعجاز خواہ طرف اعلیٰ کا ہو یا اس کے قریبی مرتبہ کا یہ دونوں متحد اور ایک ہیں بایں حیثیت کہ کلام کی یہ ایک حد ہے جو بلغ من جميع ما عداہ ہے جس کا معارضہ اور اس
…should be performed in a manner that is more eloquent and more effective than all other methods of communication. The commentator said regarding this: 'It is not an interpretation of the concept of linguistic inimitability.' That is, this is not an explanation of the meaning of i'jaz al-kalam, because i'jaz does not necessarily require eloquence. Rather, i'jaz fi al-kalam is defined as speech reaching a level where it cannot be contested and producing its like is beyond human capacity. It is derived from 'a'jaztuhu' meaning 'I rendered him incapable.' Now it is not necessary that the cause of this i'jaz be eloquence; rather, various factors can be the cause. For this reason, different reasons are given for the Quran being miraculous, despite agreement that it is miraculous. Some say it is due to its eloquence – that the Quran is miraculous because it is at a high level of eloquence beyond human reach. Some say it is due to its reports – because it contains news of the unseen, and humans cannot produce such news. This view is rejected because any surah that does not contain news of the unseen would not be miraculous, but that is incorrect; rather, every surah, even the length of a surah, is miraculous even if it does not contain news of the unseen. Some say it is due to its unique style – its style is different from the prose and poetry of the eloquent. Some say it is by Allah diverting the intellects of the opponents from contesting it. This view is also rejected because it would imply that a completely ineloquent speech could be more miraculous if contestation is merely prevented. Rather, the author's intent is to present the correct view: that the i'jaz of the Quran is based on the fact that its method of conveying meaning is more eloquent than all other methods, and its i'jaz is due to eloquence. Therefore, since i'jaz in speech requires that it be more eloquent than all other methods, that method can only be one, not multiple. Hence the term 'urwat al-i'jaz uses the singular 'urwa, unlike sihr al-kalam which uses the plural 'ahdab al-sihr. 'Urwa is stronger than hadab. The purpose is to make speech subtle and express meanings with appropriate expressions until it approaches sihr and i'jaz. Here there are two investigations: the first concerns the author's statement 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu', and the second concerns his statement 'wa la yakun hadha illa wahidan'. The summary of the first: In the definition of i'jaz as 'conveying meaning through a method more eloquent than all other methods,' what is meant by 'all other methods'? If only actual existing methods, that is insufficient for proving i'jaz, because i'jaz requires impossibility of contestation, and superiority over existing methods does not guarantee that no potential method could contest it. If it means all methods actual and potential, then being more eloquent than all is not a condition for i'jaz, because Allah is able to produce the like of the Quran, so there must be some potential method to produce its like, yet the Quran is unanimously miraculous. So what is the meaning of 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu'? The second investigation: The method of i'jaz is not singular; rather, there are multiple methods because the highest level and what is close to it are both miraculous, as mentioned in Nihayat al-I'jaz. So what is the meaning of 'la yakun illa wahidan'? The answer to the first: The second alternative is chosen – i'jaz requires being more eloquent than all actual and potential methods. Since i'jaz is only in the speech of Allah, the meaning is that compared to all methods possible in the speech of others (actual or potential), it is more eloquent, such that others cannot produce its like. Allah's ability to produce its like does not negate i'jaz. The answer to the second: I'jaz, whether at the highest level or close to it, are unified in that they represent a single limit of speech that is more eloquent than all other methods, which cannot be contested.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that expands upon the definition of i'jaz (inimitability) of the Quran as presented in the original text. The commentator first clarifies that i'jaz fundamentally means rendering others incapable of producing something similar, not necessarily through eloquence alone. He then reviews various scholarly opinions on the cause of the Quran's i'jaz: eloquence, reports of the unseen, unique style, and divine prevention (sarf). He refutes the latter two, affirming that the correct view, according to the author, is that i'jaz is due to superlative eloquence in conveying meanings. The commentator then addresses two investigations raised by this definition. The first concerns the phrase 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu' (more eloquent than all other methods): whether it refers only to actual methods or includes potential ones. He resolves that the intended meaning includes both actual and potential, but this condition is specific to the Quran as the speech of Allah, so the challenge remains. The second investigation questions why the method of i'jaz is described as singular. The commentator explains that i'jaz encompasses both the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it, but these are considered a single limit, hence the singular 'urwa. Throughout, the commentary demonstrates rigorous textual analysis consistent with Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology.

Key Terms
معارضہ (mu'arada): مقابلہ کرنا اور مثل پیش کرنا (contestation and producing a like)
صرف (sarf): اللہ تعالیٰ کا معارضین کے عقول کو پھیر دینا (Allah diverting the intellects of opponents)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi accepted cause of the Quran's i'jaz according to the commentary?
A) Reports of the unseen
B) Unique style
C) Eloquence
D) Divine prevention

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that the Quran's i'jaz stems from its superlative eloquence, refuting alternatives with logical arguments.

The Two Investigations of I'jaz
Textual analysis of the definition's implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two investigations raised by the commentator regarding the definition of i'jaz and how they are resolved.

Core Idea
The definition of i'jaz requires superiority over all actual and potential methods, yet its method remains singular.

This lesson explores the two critical investigations that the commentator addresses. The first questions whether 'all other methods' includes potential ones; the second questions why i'jaz is described as singular. Understanding these resolves apparent contradictions and solidifies the Hanafi concept of i'jaz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two investigations
First: what does 'all other methods' (jami'i ma 'adahu) mean? Second: why is i'jaz limited to one method?
These are titled al-bahth al-awwal and al-bahth al-thani.
2
Analyze the first investigation
If only actual methods, then superiority does not guarantee impossibility of contestation. If all potential methods, then Allah's ability to produce the like would negate i'jaz. The resolution: it includes potential methods specific to human capability, not divine.
The commentator chooses the second alternative but qualified: i'jaz is only in speech of Allah, so it must surpass all methods possible for others.
3
Analyze the second investigation
If there are multiple levels of eloquence (highest and close to highest), then i'jaz would have multiple methods. The resolution: both are considered a single limit because they share the quality of being beyond human capacity.
The commentator cites Nihayat al-I'jaz.
4
Understand the resolution
Both investigations are resolved by affirming that i'jaz requires being more eloquent than all methods possible for non-divine speech, and that highest and near-highest levels are unified as one limit of inimitability.
Thus the definition stands: singular method, all-encompassing superiority.

کو پیش کرنا ہے یعنی قرآن مجید کا اعجاز صحیح رای کے لحاظ سے اس پر مبنی ہے کہ ادائے معنی کا طریقہ تمام طرق اداء سے ابلغ ہے اور اس کا اعجاز بسبب بلاغت کے ہے ۔ فباعتبار انه چونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام میں شرط ہے کہ وہ اپنے جمیع ما عدا طرق سے ابلغ ہو اس لئے وه طریق واحد ہو سکتا ہے جس میں تعدد نہیں ہوتا اس لئے عروۃ الاعجاز میں لفظ عروہ واحد اختیار کیا بخلاف سحر الکلام کے کہ وہ دقت کلام اور ماخذ کے لطیف ہونے کو کہتے ہیں لہذا اس کے طرق متعددہ اور مراتب مختلفہ ہو سکتے ہیں اس لئے اہداب السحر بلفظ الجمع کہا ہرب ثوب ان پھندنوں وغیرہ کو کہا جاتا ہے جو اطراف ثوب پر ہوتے ہیں اور عروۃ الکوز اس کڑے اور دستے کو کہا جاتا ہے جس سے پکڑا جاتا ہے اویہ بنسبت ہرب کے اقوی ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو اعجاز کے ساتھ مختص کیا جو سحر سے اوثق ہوتا ہے ان کے ساتھ تمسک کرنے سے مراد کلام کو لطیف کرنے اور معانی کو عبارات لائقہ سے ادا کرنے میں مبالغہ کہ نامراد ہے یہاں تک کہ قریب الی السحر والاعجاز ہو جائے وههنا بحثان بحث اول کا تعلق مصنف کے قول ابلغ من جمیع ما عداہ کے ساتھ ہے اور بحث ثانی کا تعلق اس کے قول و لا یکون ہذا الا واحدا کے ساتھ ہے بحث اول کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اعجاز کی تفسیر میں جو یہ کہا گیا ہے کہ ان یودی المعنى بطريق هوا بلغ من جميع ما عداه من الطرق ۔ اس ما عداه من الطرق سے کیا مراد ہے اگر صرف طرق محققہ اور موجودہ مراد ہیں تو یہ اثبات اعجاز میں کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ اعجاز کے اندر ضروری ہے کہ اس کا معارضہ نا ممکن ہو اور اس کی مثل لانے سے عجز ہو اور یہ طرق محققہ موجودہ سے ابلغ ہو جانے کے ساتھ ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ طرق مقدرہ میں کوئی ایسا طریقہ ہو جس کو اختیار کر کے معارضہ کیا جاسکے اور اس کی مثل لائی جا سکے تو اعجاز ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر ما عداه من الطرق سے مراد عام ہو خواہ طرق محققہ ہوں یا مقدرہ ان جمیع سے ابلغ ہو حتیٰ کہ اس کی مثل پیش کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو یہ اعجاز میں شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالی مثل القرآن لانے پر قادر ہے تو اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ طرق مقدرہ میں کوئی ایسا طریقہ ضرور ہے جس سے مثل قرآن حاصل ہو سکتی ہے حالانکہ قرآن مجید اس احتمال کے باوجود بالاتفاق معجز ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمیع طرق محققہ و مقدرہ سے ابلغ ہونا اعجازہ میں شرط نہیں ہے فما معنی قولہ ابلغ من جميع ما عداه - والثانی اس بحث ثانی کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعجاز کا طریق صرف واحد نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے بھی متعدد طرق ہیں کیونکہ طرف اعلیٰ اور ما يقرب منہ یعنی مراتب گلیہ میں سے جو طرف اعلیٰ کے قریب ہے جس کا معارضہ اور اس کی مثل لانا بشر کے لئے ممکن نہیں یہ دونوں معجز ہیں جیسے مفتاح سکا کی اور شیخ کی نہایۃ الاعجاز میں مذکور ہے تو اس وقت طرق اعجاز بھی متعدد ہوئے بعض طرف اعلیٰ پر اور بعض اس مرتبہ پر جو قریب من الاعلیٰ ہے فما معنی قولہ لا یکون بنا الا واحدا ۔ والجواب عن الاول جواب کے اندرشق ثانی اختیار کی گئی ہے یعنی اعجاز کے اندرا بلغ من جمیع ما عداه من الطرق المحققة والمقدرة کلیتہا شرط ہے پھر چونکہ اعجاز صرف کلام اللہ میں ہے لہذا مرا من الالعجی یہ ہوگی کہ کلام غیر اللہ تعالیٰ میں جتنے طرق ادا ہو سکتے ہیں خواہ محقق ہوں یا مقدر ان تمام سے ابلغ ہو حتیٰ کہ غیر اللہ کے لئے اس کی مثل پیش کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو اب اللہ تعالیٰ کا قادر علی الاتیان بمثلہ ہونا اعجاز کے منافی نہیں ہے ۔ وعن الثانی خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ اعجاز خواہ طرف اعلیٰ کا ہو یا اس کے قریبی مرتبہ کا یہ دونوں متحد اور ایک ہیں بایں حیثیت کہ کلام کی یہ ایک حد ہے جو بلغ من جميع ما عداہ ہے جس کا معارضہ اور اس
…should be performed in a manner that is more eloquent and more effective than all other methods of communication. The commentator said regarding this: 'It is not an interpretation of the concept of linguistic inimitability.' That is, this is not an explanation of the meaning of i'jaz al-kalam, because i'jaz does not necessarily require eloquence. Rather, i'jaz fi al-kalam is defined as speech reaching a level where it cannot be contested and producing its like is beyond human capacity. It is derived from 'a'jaztuhu' meaning 'I rendered him incapable.' Now it is not necessary that the cause of this i'jaz be eloquence; rather, various factors can be the cause. For this reason, different reasons are given for the Quran being miraculous, despite agreement that it is miraculous. Some say it is due to its eloquence – that the Quran is miraculous because it is at a high level of eloquence beyond human reach. Some say it is due to its reports – because it contains news of the unseen, and humans cannot produce such news. This view is rejected because any surah that does not contain news of the unseen would not be miraculous, but that is incorrect; rather, every surah, even the length of a surah, is miraculous even if it does not contain news of the unseen. Some say it is due to its unique style – its style is different from the prose and poetry of the eloquent. Some say it is by Allah diverting the intellects of the opponents from contesting it. This view is also rejected because it would imply that a completely ineloquent speech could be more miraculous if contestation is merely prevented. Rather, the author's intent is to present the correct view: that the i'jaz of the Quran is based on the fact that its method of conveying meaning is more eloquent than all other methods, and its i'jaz is due to eloquence. Therefore, since i'jaz in speech requires that it be more eloquent than all other methods, that method can only be one, not multiple. Hence the term 'urwat al-i'jaz uses the singular 'urwa, unlike sihr al-kalam which uses the plural 'ahdab al-sihr. 'Urwa is stronger than hadab. The purpose is to make speech subtle and express meanings with appropriate expressions until it approaches sihr and i'jaz. Here there are two investigations: the first concerns the author's statement 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu', and the second concerns his statement 'wa la yakun hadha illa wahidan'. The summary of the first: In the definition of i'jaz as 'conveying meaning through a method more eloquent than all other methods,' what is meant by 'all other methods'? If only actual existing methods, that is insufficient for proving i'jaz, because i'jaz requires impossibility of contestation, and superiority over existing methods does not guarantee that no potential method could contest it. If it means all methods actual and potential, then being more eloquent than all is not a condition for i'jaz, because Allah is able to produce the like of the Quran, so there must be some potential method to produce its like, yet the Quran is unanimously miraculous. So what is the meaning of 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu'? The second investigation: The method of i'jaz is not singular; rather, there are multiple methods because the highest level and what is close to it are both miraculous, as mentioned in Nihayat al-I'jaz. So what is the meaning of 'la yakun illa wahidan'? The answer to the first: The second alternative is chosen – i'jaz requires being more eloquent than all actual and potential methods. Since i'jaz is only in the speech of Allah, the meaning is that compared to all methods possible in the speech of others (actual or potential), it is more eloquent, such that others cannot produce its like. Allah's ability to produce its like does not negate i'jaz. The answer to the second: I'jaz, whether at the highest level or close to it, are unified in that they represent a single limit of speech that is more eloquent than all other methods, which cannot be contested.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that expands upon the definition of i'jaz (inimitability) of the Quran as presented in the original text. The commentator first clarifies that i'jaz fundamentally means rendering others incapable of producing something similar, not necessarily through eloquence alone. He then reviews various scholarly opinions on the cause of the Quran's i'jaz: eloquence, reports of the unseen, unique style, and divine prevention (sarf). He refutes the latter two, affirming that the correct view, according to the author, is that i'jaz is due to superlative eloquence in conveying meanings. The commentator then addresses two investigations raised by this definition. The first concerns the phrase 'ablaghu min jami'i ma 'adahu' (more eloquent than all other methods): whether it refers only to actual methods or includes potential ones. He resolves that the intended meaning includes both actual and potential, but this condition is specific to the Quran as the speech of Allah, so the challenge remains. The second investigation questions why the method of i'jaz is described as singular. The commentator explains that i'jaz encompasses both the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it, but these are considered a single limit, hence the singular 'urwa. Throughout, the commentary demonstrates rigorous textual analysis consistent with Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology.

Key Terms
بحث (bahth): تحقیق اور غور و فکر (investigation; a point of scholarly inquiry)
طریق محققة ومقدرة (turuq muhagqaqa wa muqaddara): موجودہ اور ممکنہ طرق (actual and potential methods)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the singular description of i'jaz not contradict the existence of near-highest levels of eloquence?
A) Because only the highest level is truly i'jaz.
B) Because both highest and near-highest are beyond human capacity, forming a single limit.
C) Because the near-highest is not actually miraculous.
D) Because the author used the plural incorrectly.

Key Takeaway
The two investigations ensure that i'jaz covers all human potential and that its singularity refers to a single boundary beyond which human capacity cannot reach.

Definition of the Quran in Hanafi Usul
Introducing the two-part structure of the work and defining the Quran as the first source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran and explain why it excludes other scriptures and hadith qudsi.

Core Idea
The Quran is the mutawatir transmitted text between the covers of the 'Uthmanic codices, excluding all other divine words.

This passage marks the beginning of a detailed discussion of the sources of Shari'ah. The author first outlines the structure of the work, dividing it into two parts. The first part deals with the four pillars of evidence: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. The first pillar is the Book, which is then defined as the Quran. The commentator expands on this definition, providing the precise criteria that distinguish the Quran from other revelations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
The passage states the book is divided into two parts; the first part is on Shari'ah and has four pillars.
2
Focus on the first pillar
The first pillar is 'Kitab', which is equated with the Quran.
3
Analyze the definition of the Quran
The definition includes two key elements: transmission between the covers of the codices and tawatur.
4
Understand what is excluded
The definition excludes earlier scriptures (Torah, Gospel) and other hadiths (qudsi, prophetic).
Exclusion is based on the requirement of tawatur and the physical compilation in the 'Uthmanic codices.

Source Text

قال المصنف في التوضح فنضع الكتاب على قسمین پس ہم نے اس کتاب کی وضع دو قسموں پر رکھی ہے القسم الاول پہلی قسم اولہ شرعیہ میں ہے اور یہ ارکان اربعہ پر مبنی ہے۔ کیونکہ ادلہ چار ہیں کتاب - سنہ - اجتماع ۔ قیاس ۔ الركن الأول في الكتاب الى القرآن لفظ القران یہ تفسیر ہے الکتاب کی بلفظ اشهر وهو ما نقل الينا الخزيه القرآن کی تعریف ہے بین دفتی ای جانبی المصاحف مصاحف سے مراد وہ مصاحف ہیں جو حضرت عثمان رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ نے جمع کرائے پھر ان کے بعد جو ان کے موافق مکتوب ہو کر پھیلے تو اترا اور منقول بنقل متواتر ہو نخرج سائر الكتب الالهية كالتوراة والانجيل والاحادیث الالهية كالاحاديث القدسيه والنبويه اى اقوال
The author said in Al-Tawdih: 'We place the book on two divisions.' So we have placed this book on two divisions. The first division is in Shari'ah and is based on four pillars because the evidences are four: the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. The first pillar is the Book, i.e., the Quran. 'Kitab' is interpreted by the more famous word 'Quran'. It is that which has been transmitted to us... The definition of the Quran is: between the two covers, i.e., the sides of the codices (masahif). Masahif refer to those codices that 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) collected, and then after him, what was written in accordance with them and spread, and was transmitted by mutawatir transmission. It excludes other divine books like the Torah and the Gospel, and divine hadiths like hadith qudsi and prophetic sayings.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new section in the commentary (sharh) on Al-Tawdih. The commentator explains the author's statement that the book is divided into two parts, though only the first part is detailed here. The first part deals with the Shari'ah (Islamic law) and is built on four pillars: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). The commentator then focuses on the first pillar: the Book, which is interpreted as the Quran. The Quran is defined as that which is transmitted to us between the covers of the codices (masahif) that were compiled under the caliph 'Uthman and later transmitted via mutawatir (massively recurrent) chains. This definition excludes earlier scriptures like the Torah and Gospel, as well as hadith qudsi and prophetic hadith, because they are not transmitted with the same textual form and tawatur. This definition is standard in Hanafi usul to distinguish the Quran from other revelations.

Key Terms
الكتاب (al-Kitab): In this context, it refers to the Quran, the first source of Shari'ah.
القرآن (al-Quran): The revealed word of Allah transmitted between the two covers of the masahif via tawatur, excluding all other scriptures and hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the definition of the Quran exclude hadith qudsi?
A) Because hadith qudsi is not between the covers of the 'Uthmanic codices.
B) Because hadith qudsi is not transmitted via tawatur.
C) Because hadith qudsi is not Arabic.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is defined by its mutawatir transmission and physical compilation in the 'Uthmanic codices, making it the primary and most authoritative source of Shari'ah.

Al-Quran as Source

Defining the Quran and Refuting Circularity
Definition of the Quran with exclusion and refutation of circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran, apply its exclusion criteria, and explain why Ibn al-Hajib's circularity objection fails.

Core Idea
The Quran is what is transmitted mutawatir in the Uthmani Mushaf; the Mushaf is known by custom, breaking circularity.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the definition of the Quran is foundational: it determines which texts carry absolute authority. The passage presents a precise definition, excludes other scriptures and irregular readings, and defends against a charge of circularity raised by Ibn al-Hajib. Understanding this definition and its defense sharpens your skill in handling definitions and critiques in usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the passage and extract the exact definition: the Quran is what has been transmitted mutawatir between the covers of the Mushaf compiled by Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him).
The phrase 'ما نقل إلينا بين دفتي المصاحف التي جمعها عثمان' is the core.
2
Analyze the exclusions
Note what is excluded: other divine books (Torah, Gospel), hadith qudsi, prophetic hadiths, and irregular qira'at. Identify the reason for each exclusion.
Irregular qira'at are excluded because they lack tawatur.
3
Understand the circularity objection
Ibn al-Hajib argues that defining Quran by Mushaf requires knowing Mushaf, and defining Mushaf as 'that in which the Quran is written' creates a circle.
The objection is based on the interdependence of definitions.
4
Apply the refutation
The author refutes by stating that the Mushaf is known by custom ('urf), so it does not need definition; thus knowledge of Quran depends on Mushaf, but knowledge of Mushaf does not depend on Quran.
This breaks the circularity.

Source Text

الدور ہے لانه عرف القرآن بر لزوم دور کی دلیل ہے حاصل یہ کہ قرآن کی تعریف ما نقل في المصحف کی گئی ہے تو معرفت قرآن معرفت مصحف پر موقوف ہو گئی لہذا معرفت مصحف ضروری ہے ورنہ تو ماہیتہ قرآن واضح نہیں ہوگی دان سئل اور اگر مصحف کی معرفت کے متعلق سوال کیا جائے اور کہا جائے ما المصحف تو لامحالہ جواب میبی ہو گا الذي كتب فيه القران تو معرفت مصحف معرفت قرآن پر موقوف ہوگئی تو سہی دور ہے یعنی توقف الشتي على ما يتوقف على ذلك الشئی تو یہاں بھی ایسے ہے کہ معرفت قران موقوف على معرفة المصحف ہوئی اور معرفت مصحف موقوف علی معرفت القرآن ہوئی بل ہذا الادور ناجبت عن هذا بقولی ولا دور یعنی قرآن کی تعریف مذکور مشتمل على الدور نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرآن کی معرفت تو موقوف علی معرفت المصحف ہے لیکن مصحف کی معرفت موقوف علی معرفت القرآن نہیں ہے لان المصحف معلوم في العرف یعنی لوگوں کے عرف میں مصحف معلوم اور متعارف ہے اور لوگ جانتے پہچانتے اس لئے یہ محتاج الى التعریف نہیں ہے جو کہ الذی کتب فیہ القرآن کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے قال الشارح في التلويح قوله فنضع تفريع على قوله نحث الخ یعنی فنضع کی تفریح یجٹ پر ہے یعنی چونکہ اس فن میں ادلہ اور احکام سے بحث ہوتی ہے اس لئے ہم اپنی کتاب کی وضع دو قسموں پر کر رہے ہیں قسم اول ادلہ میں ہوگی اور قسم ثانی احکام میں اعتراض وارد ہوتا تھا کہ اس کتاب میں مبحث تعریف اور مبحث موضوع بھی درج ہے جو ان قسموں کے علاوہ ہے تو پھر مجموع کتاب کی وضع صرف قسمین پر تو نہیں ہے پھر یہ نضع علی قمین کیسے صحیح ہو گا تو شارح نے مقاصدہ کا لفظ ذکر کر کے اس اعتراض کو مرتفع کیا یعنی مقاصد کتاب قسمین میں منحصر ہیں نہ کہ مجموع کتاب کیونکہ مبحث تعریف و موضوع کتاب میں داخل ہے اور قیمین سے خارج ہے تو حصر فی القسمین نہ رہا تو اس کا جواب ديا لكونه غير داخل في المقاصد یعنی یہ مقاصد میں سے نہیں اور ہم نے مقاصد کتاب کو قسمین پر موضوع کیا ہے لہذا ان مباحث
The author said in Al-Tawdih: So we divide the book into two sections. So we have placed the division of this book into two sections. The first section is in Islamic legal principles and is based on four pillars. Because the proofs are four: Book, Sunnah, Consensus, Analogy. The first pillar: On the Book, meaning the Quran. The word Quran is an interpretation of 'al-Kitab' by the more famous word, and it is what has been transmitted to us ... The definition of the Quran is: 'between the covers' i.e., the sides of the Mushaf. By Mushaf is meant those Mushafs which Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) compiled, then after him, whatever is written in accordance with them and spread, revealed, and transmitted with mutawatir transmission. It excludes all other divine books like Torah and Gospel, and divine hadiths like hadith qudsi and prophetic hadiths i.e., statements of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); all these are excluded from the definition because they are not transmitted between the covers of the Mushaf. Also, irregular Qira'at are excluded because their transmission is not mutawatir; rather they are found in some specific Mushafs like the Mushaf of Ibn Mas'ud or Ubayy bin Ka'b (may Allah be pleased with them), their transmission is not mutawatir but by ahad reports. Ibn al-Hajib raised an objection that this definition contains circularity because it defines the Quran as what is transmitted in the Mushaf, so knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the Mushaf, then if asked 'what is the Mushaf?' the answer would be 'that in which the Quran is written', so knowledge of the Mushaf depends on knowledge of the Quran. Thus circularity occurs. The author responds: there is no circularity because knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the Mushaf, but knowledge of the Mushaf does not depend on knowledge of the Quran, because the Mushaf is known in common usage ('urf). People know what the Mushaf is, so it does not need definition. The commentator in Al-Talwih said: His statement 'so we divide' is a branching from his statement 'we discuss' etc. So 'so we divide' is a branching from 'we discuss' meaning because in this discipline the discussion is about proofs and rulings, so we place the division of our book into two sections: the first section will be on proofs, and the second section on rulings. An objection was raised: In this book, the discussion of definition and subject matter is also included, which is apart from these two sections, so the total book is not only two sections, then how is 'we divide into two sections' correct? The commentator answered by mentioning the word 'objectives' (maqasid): the objectives of the book are confined to two sections, not the entire book, because the discussion of definition and subject matter is included in the book but outside the two sections, so the restriction to two sections is not maintained. Then he answered: because it is not included in the objectives, and we have placed the objectives of the book into two sections, so those discussions are outside the objectives.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the Quran from the perspective of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) defines the Quran as what is transmitted mutawatir between the covers of the Mushaf compiled by Uthman. This excludes earlier scriptures, hadith qudsi, and irregular qira'at. Ibn al-Hajib objects that this definition is circular, but the author refutes by noting that the Mushaf is known by common custom ('urf), so it does not require definition. The commentator (Taftazani in Al-Talwih) further clarifies that the division of the book into two sections (proofs and rulings) refers to its objectives, not the entire content, thus the preliminary discussions of definition and subject matter are outside the main objectives.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-Qur'an): The transmitted text between the covers of the Uthmani Mushaf via tawatur.
المصحف (al-Mushaf): The physical book containing the Quranic text, specifically the Uthmani codex.
الدور (al-dawr): Circularity in definition, where one term is defined by another which in turn is defined by the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for rejecting the charge of circularity in the definition of the Quran according to the passage?
A) The Mushaf is defined by the Quran.
B) The Quran is known by its miraculous nature.
C) The Mushaf is known by common custom ('urf).
D) The definition is based on tawatur alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran avoids circularity by relying on the Mushaf's known status in custom, and excludes all texts not transmitted mutawatir within the Uthmani codex.

6 min
Refuting the Charge of Circularity in the Definition of the Quran
Critique and defense of defining Quran as transmitted in mus-haf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical objection of dawr (circularity) and apply the Hanafi response based on urf to defend the definition of the Quran.

Core Idea
A definition is only circular if both terms depend on each other; the mus-haf is known by custom, breaking the loop.

Ibn al-Hajib raised a powerful objection: if the Quran is defined as 'what is transmitted in the mus-haf', and the mus-haf is defined as 'that in which the Quran is written', the definition is circular. The Hanafi school replies that the mus-haf is independently known through everyday custom (urf), so the definition holds. This lesson unpacks the argument and its implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
Identify exactly what Ibn al-Hajib claimed: the definition of Quran as 'what is transmitted in the mus-haf' leads to circularity.
The objection is a logical critique common in usul.
2
Analyze the supposed circularity
Note that knowledge of Quran depends on mus-haf, and if asked 'what is mus-haf', the answer would be 'that in which Quran is written', creating a dependency loop.
This is the classical dawr (circularity) argument.
3
Present the Hanafi response
The mus-haf is known through common custom (urf), not through a definition that mentions the Quran. Thus, no real circularity.
The response hinges on the epistemological independence of urf.
4
Evaluate the strength of urf in this context
Recognize that urf is an accepted source of knowledge in Hanafi usul; it provides independent knowledge of the mus-haf.
Other schools may give less weight to urf in definitional matters.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand that accepting this definition affects which readings are considered Quranic: only those transmitted mutawatir in the standard mus-haf.
Excludes anomalous readings (qira'at shadhdhah) not in the standard mus-haf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم یہ تمام کے تمام خارج از تعریف ہو گئے کیونکہ یہ منقول بین دفتی المصاحف نہیں ہیں والقرات الشاذة کیونکہ ان کی نقل بالتواتر نہیں بلکہ یہ بعض مصاحف مخصوصہ میں ہیں جیسے مصحف ابن مسعود یا ابی بن کعب رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کہ ان کی نقل بالتواتر نہیں ہے بلکہ باخبار الاحاد ہے وقد اور د ابن الحاجب ابن حاجب نے اعتراض وارد کیا ہے کہ ان هذا التعريف دوری یہ تعریف مشتمل على الدور ہے لانه عرف القرآن بر لزوم دور کی دلیل ہے حاصل یہ کہ قرآن کی تعریف ما نقل في المصحف کی گئی ہے تو معرفت قرآن معرفت مصحف پر موقوف ہو گئی لہذا معرفت مصحف ضروری ہے ورنہ تو ماہیتہ قرآن واضح نہیں ہوگی دان سئل اور اگر مصحف کی معرفت کے متعلق سوال کیا جائے اور کہا جائے ما المصحف تو لامحالہ جواب میبی ہو گا الذي كتب فيه القران تو معرفت مصحف معرفت قرآن پر موقوف ہوگئی تو سہی دور ہے یعنی توقف الشتي على ما يتوقف على ذلك الشئی تو یہاں بھی ایسے ہے کہ معرفت قران موقوف على معرفة المصحف ہوئی اور معرفت مصحف موقوف علی معرفة القرآن ہوئی بل ہذا الادور ناجبت عن هذا بقولی ولا دور یعنی قرآن کی تعریف مذکور مشتمل على الدور نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرآن کی معرفت تو موقوف علی معرفت المصحف ہے لیکن مصحف کی معرفت موقوف علی معرفت القرآن نہیں ہے لان المصحف معلوم في العرف یعنی لوگوں کے عرف میں مصحف معلوم اور متعارف ہے اور لوگ جانتے پہچانتے اس لئے یہ محتاج الى التعریف نہیں ہے جو کہ الذی کتب فیہ القرآن کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے
Those who transmitted the Quran (the Companions) all fall outside the definition because they are not transmitted between the two covers of the mus-haf. As for the anomalous readings, because their transmission is not mutawatir; rather they are in specific mus-hafs like the mus-haf of Ibn Mas'ud or Ubayy ibn Ka'b (may Allah be pleased with them), their transmission is not mutawatir but by khabar al-ahad. Ibn al-Hajib has raised an objection that this definition contains circularity. The summary is that the Quran is defined as 'what is transmitted in the mus-haf'. So knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the mus-haf. Therefore knowledge of the mus-haf is necessary, otherwise the essence of the Quran would not be clear. If one asks about knowledge of the mus-haf 'what is the mus-haf?', inevitably the answer would be 'that in which the Quran is written'. So knowledge of the mus-haf would depend on knowledge of the Quran, thus circularity arises, i.e., the dependence of a thing on that which depends on that thing. I replied to this by saying: There is no circularity. Because knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the mus-haf, but knowledge of the mus-haf does not depend on knowledge of the Quran, because the mus-haf is known in custom (urf). That is, in people's custom the mus-haf is known and familiar, and people recognize it. So it does not need definition, nor does it need the definition 'that in which the Quran is written'.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a critique by Ibn al-Hajib of the Hanafi definition of the Quran as 'what is transmitted in the mus-haf'. Ibn al-Hajib argues that this definition is circular because to know the Quran one must know the mus-haf, but to know the mus-haf one must know the Quran. The commentator refutes this by invoking custom (urf): the mus-haf is commonly known among people without needing a definition referencing the Quran. Thus the definition is sound. This is a typical Hanafi position that relies on urf as a valid source of knowledge in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circularity in definition where each term depends on the other.
مصحف (mus-haf): The codex containing the written Quran, known by custom.
عرف (urf): Commonly known custom; a recognised source of knowledge in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the definition of the Quran as 'what is transmitted in the mus-haf' not circular?
A) Because the mus-haf is defined by revelation
B) Because the mus-haf is known by custom (urf)
C) Because the Quran is defined by mus-haf
D) Because the definition is taken from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran as 'transmitted in the mus-haf' is not circular because the mus-haf is independently known through custom (urf).

Defining Kitab and Qur'an in Hanafi Usul
Defines Kitab and Qur'an linguistically and technically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul definition of both 'Kitab' and 'Qur'an' and explain why the author interprets 'Kitab' as 'Qur'an'.

Core Idea
Kitab and Qur'an are technically synonymous in Hanafi usul, but the definition applies primarily to the Qur'an as revealed, written speech.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwiih clarifies the precise definitions of 'Kitab' and 'Qur'an' as used by Hanafi usul scholars. You will learn how these terms are distinguished from linguistic and theological usages, and why the author chooses to define Kitab through the better-known term Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definitions
Note that 'Kitab' linguistically means 'written thing', while 'Qur'an' is a verbal noun meaning 'recitation'.
These base meanings differ from the technical usul definitions.
2
Analyze the Sharia definition of Kitab
In Sharia, 'Kitab' refers specifically to the Book of Allah written in the mus-haf, just as grammarians use 'al-Kitab' for Sibawayh's book.
This is a technical specialization (nagl).
3
Understand why the author interprets Kitab as Qur'an
The term 'Qur'an' is more famous and clear in common usage. Therefore the author says 'i.e. the Qur'an' to avoid ambiguity.
This shows the author's pedagogical aim.
4
Parse the full definitional phrase
The phrase 'al-Kitab is the Qur'an revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-haf' is not a definition of Kitab (which would be circular), but rather 'al-Qur'an' interprets Kitab and the rest defines the Qur'an.
This resolves the apparent tautology.
5
Identify the essential attributes
The definition includes revelation (inzal) and being written in the mus-haf. Other attributes like miraculousness and mutawatir transmission are discussed but not essential for the author's purpose.
The author suffices with the minimal attributes to distinguish from other books.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کو مقاصد کتاب سے خارج رہنا چاہیئے لہذا مقاصد کتاب کی وضع على القسمين رہی البتہ مجموع کتنا میں تو درج ہیں القسم الاول مرتب الخ قسم اول چار ارکان پر مرتب ہے جو ادلہ اربعہ میں ہیں پہلا کتاب میں پھر سنہ پھر اجماع پھر قیاس میں جو بالذات اور یا لشرف مقدم تھی ذكر أو وضعاً اسی کو مقدم کیا گیا ہے باقی رہے آخری دو باب ایک باب الترجیح دوسرا باب الاجتہاد یہ ادله سے الگ مبحث نہیں بلکہ رکن قیاس کا یہ تمہ اور تذبیل ہے یعنی قیاس کا ذیل اور دامن ہیں لہذا یہ دونوں باب درج في القياس میں قولہ الركن الاول في الكتاب دهو الى الكتاب في اللغة اسم المكتوب لغت میں تو کتاب نام ہے مکتوب اور لکھی ہوئی کا اور عرف شریعت الکتاب کے زیادہ مشہور اور اظہر ہے اس لیے مصنف نے القرآن کو لفظ الکتاب کی تفسیر بنا کر کہا ای القرآن لہذا کہا جاتا ہے الكتاب هو القران المنزل على الرسول کے زیادہ مشہور کی تفسیر بنا کر کہا ای القرآن ہذا اصطلاح میں القرآن کا اطلاق اس وصف قدیم پر ہوتا ہے جو غیر مخلوق ہے اور اصولیین کے نزدیک ان کا اطلاق مجموع من حیث المجموع اور ہر ہر جز پر جو دلیل علی الحکم ہو سکے ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ حضرات کتاب اللہ سے بحیثیت دلیل علی الحکم ہونے کے بحث کرتے ہیں اور یہ آیت آیت دلیل کا کام دیتی ہے نہ صرف مجموع من حيث المجموع فاحتاجوا تو یہ اصولیین اس طرف محتاج ہوتے کہ صفات مشترکہ بین الکل والجزر کی جستجو کریں تاکہ انھیں تعریف میں استعمال کریں جو کہ مجموع پر اور جز پر صادق آسکے مثلا معجز ہونا منزل علی الرسول ہونا مکتوب فی المصاحف ہونا منقول بالنقل المتواتر ہونا یہ ایسے صفات ہیں جو علی السویہ کل اور جز میں مشترک ہیں بعض حضرات نے بقصد توضیح ان جمیع صفات کو تعریف و تفسیر میں اعتبار کیا اور بعض حضرات نے صرف انزال اور اعجاز کواء کیا کیونکہ قرآن مجید کے ہر دور میں یہی صفات لازمہ ہیں بخلاف کتابت و نقل کے کہ رسول اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں قرآن مجيد مكتوب في المصاحف اور منقول الینا کے بغیر متحقق تھا لہذا یہ صفات غیر لازمہ ہیں ان کو تعریف میں استعمال نہ کیا جائے وبعضهم الانزال والكتابه والنقل لان المقصود يعني قرآن مجید کی تعریف سے مقصود اصلی ان لوگوں کے لئے تعریف کرتا ہے جنہوں نے وحی کا مشاہدہ کیا اور نہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا زمانہ پایا تو وہ لوگ قرآن مجید کو نقل اور کتابت فی المصاحف سے جانتے ہیں اور ان کے زمانہ میں یہ لوازم غیر منفکہ ہیں تو یہ ان کے لئے آئین اللوازم ہیں اور دلالۃ علی المقصود میں اوضح ہیں لہذا ان کے لئے ان لوازم کے ساتھ تعریف کرنا مفید ہے بخلاف الاعجاز الخ بخلاف اعجاز کے کہ یہ ان لوگوں کے لئے لوازم بینہ سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ معرفت اعجاز تو مخصوص علماء کا کام ہے جو ماہر فی علم المعانی والبیان ہوں۔ ولا الشاملۃ اور یہ ہر جز کو بھی شامل نہیں کیونکہ معجره تو صرف سورۃ ہے یا اس کی مقدار کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فاتوا بسورۃ من مثلہ اسی پر دال ہے۔ والمصنف اقتصر على ذكر الو مصنف نے نقل في المصاحف تو اترا کے ذکر پر اکتفا کیا ہے کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ مقصد تعریف پورا ہو جاتا ہے اور جمیع ماعدا القران سے احتراز حاصل ہو جاتا ہے لان سائر الكتب السماوية الخ کيونکہ قران مجید کے علاوہ باقی تمام کتب سماویہ وغیرنا
The author says: The first pillar is about Kitab. Kitab linguistically means written matter. In Sharia, it is used for the Book of Allah, which is written in the mus-haf. Just as in the terminology of grammarians, 'al-Kitab' predominantly refers to Sibawayh's book. And 'Qur'an' linguistically is a verbal noun meaning recitation, but in common usage it predominantly refers to the specific collection of Allah's speech that is recited by the worshippers. This meaning is more famous and apparent than 'al-Kitab'. Therefore, the author interprets 'al-Kitab' as 'al-Qur'an', saying 'i.e. the Qur'an'. So it is said: 'al-Kitab is the Qur'an revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-haf.' Thus 'al-Qur'an' is an interpretation of 'al-Kitab', and the remaining part 'revealed to the Messenger' is a definition of the Qur'an, distinguishing it from other things. However, this entire expression is not the definition of Kitab, otherwise there would be the problem of al-dhikr al-mahdud fi al-hadd, because the Qur'an is another name for Kitab. There is no need to interpret the word 'Qur'an' as 'al-muqarr' to include divine and non-divine speech, as done by some. This interpretation, though linguistically valid, contradicts the common usage and is far from the way of the earlier scholars. Although such critiques are not applied to the expressions of the early scholars because they focused only on purposes, not on wording, still there is no reason to force their words into a weak interpretation when there is a clear correct explanation: that 'al-Qur'an' is an interpretation of 'al-Kitab', and the rest is a definition of the Qur'an. To remove this misunderstanding, the author explicitly uses the particle of interpretation, saying 'i.e. the Qur'an, and it is what has been transmitted to us…' Both 'al-Kitab' and 'al-Qur'an' are used by usul scholars in a specific sense, contrary to the theologians (mutakallimun) who apply 'al-Qur'an' to the eternal attribute. According to usul scholars, these terms apply both to the whole and to every part that can serve as evidence for a ruling, because they discuss the Book of Allah as evidence, and every verse serves as evidence. So they need to find common attributes between the whole and the part, such as being miraculous, revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-haf, and transmitted mutawatir. Some scholars consider all these attributes in the definition, while others consider only revelation and inimitability because these are essential in every era, unlike being written and transmitted, which were not present in the Prophet's time. Some consider revelation, writing, and transmission because the purpose of the definition is for those who did not witness revelation or the Prophet's time; for them, these attributes are inseparable and clearer. Inimitability is not clear for them because it is known only by experts in rhetoric, and it does not include every part (since inimitability exists only in a sura or its equivalent, as per the verse 'bring a sura like it'). The author sufficed with mentioning revelation and writing in the mus-haf because the purpose of definition is achieved and it excludes all other heavenly books.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definitional analysis of the terms 'Kitab' and 'Qur'an' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author (commentator on al-Tawdih) explains that the first pillar of the four sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) is Kitab. He begins by noting that the word 'Kitab' linguistically means 'written thing', but in Sharia it is used specifically for the Qur'an written in the mus-haf. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) interprets 'al-Kitab' as 'al-Qur'an' because the term Qur'an is more famous and clear. The definition of Kitab is thus: 'the Qur'an revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-haf, transmitted to us via tawatur'. However, this entire phrase is not a definition of Kitab per se; rather, 'al-Qur'an' interprets Kitab, and the rest (revealed, written, transmitted) defines the Qur'an. The commentator then addresses a potential misunderstanding: if the whole phrase were the definition of Kitab, it would be circular because Kitab is being defined by Qur'an which is its synonym. He rejects alternative interpretations that would take 'Qur'an' in its linguistic meaning of 'al-muqarr' (to include non-Islamic scriptures) because that contradicts the technical usage. Instead, he clarifies that the author's construction is: 'Kitab is the Qur'an' (where Qur'an is a well-known proper name), and then the attributes describe that Qur'an. The passage also highlights a key difference between usul scholars and mutakallimun: usul scholars apply the term 'Qur'an' to both the whole collection and every individual part (verse) that serves as evidence, whereas theologians restrict it to the eternal attribute of speech, which is not divisible. This difference stems from the usul scholars' need to treat each verse as a separate proof. Consequently, there is an internal debate among usul scholars about which attributes to include in the definition: some include all common attributes (miraculousness, revelation, being written, mutawatir transmission), while others include only revelation and miraculousness because writing and transmission were not present during the Prophet's lifetime. Still others include writing and transmission as well, because later generations rely on these to know the Qur'an, and miraculousness is not immediately apparent to everyone. The author (of this commentary) notes that Sadr al-Shariah (the original matn author) sufficed with mentioning revelation and writing in the mus-haf, as that excludes all other divine books and suffices for the definition's purpose.

Key Terms
الكتاب (al-Kitab): The Qur'an revealed to the Prophet, written in the mus-haf, and transmitted mutawatir.
القرآن (al-Qur'an): The specific divine speech revealed to Muhammad, miraculous in nature, written in the mus-haf, and mutawatir in transmission.
المنزل على الرسول (al-munazzal 'ala al-rasul): Revealed to the Messenger Muhammad, distinguishing it from divine speech revealed to other prophets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul definition, why does the author interpret 'al-Kitab' as 'al-Qur'an'?
A) Because 'Kitab' is a broader term that includes all scriptures.
B) Because 'Qur'an' is more famous and clear in common usage.
C) Because 'Kitab' linguistically means 'written' while 'Qur'an' means 'recited'.
D) Because the author wanted to avoid tautology.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul definition of 'Kitab' and 'Qur'an' must apply to every part (verse) to allow each verse to serve as independent legal evidence.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Usuli Definition of the Quran: Scope and Attributes
Usul al-fiqh definition of the Quran with commentary on required attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the usuli definition of the Quran, identify the necessary attributes for a definition, and explain why different scholars prioritize different sets.

Core Idea
The usuli definition must apply to every single verse, not just the whole Qur'an.

This lesson examines how usul al-fiqh scholars define the Quran, focusing on the criteria that make a definition inclusive of both the entire compilation and each individual verse. The passage discusses various attributes such as revelation, inimitability, written form, and tawatur, and why the author simplified the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and perspective
The Quran is being defined from the perspective of usul al-fiqh, not theology. For usulis, the definition must apply to both the whole collection and every part that serves as evidence for a ruling.
Distinguish from the theological definition as the eternal attribute.
2
List proposed attributes and classify them
Attributes like being revealed (inzal), miraculous (i'jaz), written in mushafs, transmitted by tawatur, etc., are proposed. Some are necessary (lazim) at all times; others (like writing in mushafs) are not necessary at the time of revelation.
Consider why some scholars include writing and tawatur even though they were absent at revelation.
3
Understand the author's simplification
The author sufficed with 'transmitted in the mushafs' because it achieves the purpose of excluding non-Quranic materials (previous scriptures, hadith qudsi, abrogated verses, etc.) and is clear for later generations.
Tawatur is implicitly included via 'transmitted'.
4
Test the definition with counterexamples
Apply the definition to irregular recitations (qira'at shadhdhah): they are not transmitted by tawatur, so they are excluded. Similarly, hadith qudsi and abrogated recitation verses are not transmitted in the mushafs.
This shows the definition effectively distinguishes Quran from non-Quran.
5
Explain why inzāl and i'jāz are omitted
Inzāl is already implied by 'Quran' as revealed speech; i'jāz is not required for the common believer who relies on transmission and writing. Hence the author left them out.
This is a practical definition for the purpose of identifying the Quran as evidence.

تصریح کرتے ہوئے كہا [تعریف] القرآن و هو ما نقل إلينا التام كل من الكتاب والقرآن يطلق عند الأصوليين يعني اصول فقہ والوں کے نزدیک بخلاف علم الکلام کے کہ ان کی اصطلاح میں القرآن کا اطلاق اس وصف قدیم پر اور جز پر صادق آسکے مثلا معجز ہونا منزل علی الرسول ہونا مكتوب فى المصاحف ہونا منقول بالنقل المتواتر ہونا یہ ایسے صفات ہیں جو علی السویہ کل اور جز میں مشترک ہیں بعض حضرات نے بقصد توضیح ان جمیع صفات کو تعریف و تفسیر میں اعتبار کیا اور بعض حضرات نے صرف انزال اور اعجاز کو کیا کیونکہ قرآن مجید کے ہر دور میں یہی صفات لازمہ ہیں بخلاف کتابت و نقل کے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں قرآن مجيد مكتوب في المصاحف اور منقول الینا کے بغیر متحقق تھا لہذا یہ صفات غیر لازمہ ہیں ان کو تعریف میں استعمال نہ کیا جائے وبعضهم الانزال والكتابه والنقل لان المقصود يعني قرآن مجید کی تعریف سے مقصود اصلی ان لوگوں کے لئے تعریف کرتا ہے جنہوں نے وحی کا مشاہدہ کیا اور نہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا زمانہ پایا تو وہ لوگ قرآن مجید کو نقل اور کتابت فی المصاحف سے جانتے ہیں اور ان کے زمانہ میں یہ لوازم غیر منفکہ ہیں تو یہ ان کے لئے آئین اللوازم ہیں اور دلالۃ علی المقصود میں اوضح ہیں لہذا ان کے لئے ان لوازم کے ساتھ تعریف کرنا مفید ہے بخلاف الاعجاز الخ بخلاف اعجاز کے کہ یہ ان لوگوں کے لئے لوازم بینہ سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ معرفت اعجاز تو مخصوص علماء کا کام ہے جو ماہر فی علم المعانی والبیان ہوں۔ ولا الشاملۃ اور یہ ہر جز کو بھی شامل نہیں کیونکہ معجره تو صرف سورۃ ہے یا اس کی مقدار کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول جاتا ہے لان سائر الكتب السماوية الخ كيونکہ قران مجید کے علاوہ باقی تمام کتب سماویہ وغیرنا سے کوئی اور احادیث الھیہ قدسیہ اور منسوخ التلاوة آیات اور احادیث نبویہ ان مں [؟] منقول بين دفتي المصاحف نہیں ہے لانه اسم لهذا المعهود الخ كيونكہ قرآن مجید اس معہود اور متعین مجموعہ کا نام ہے جو معلوم اور متعارف عند الناس ہے حتی کہ صبیان و اطفال بھی اسے جانتے پہچانتے ہیں اور تمام مذکورات اس مصحف متعارف میں منقول نہیں ہیں والقرات الشاذة اور قرآت شازہ تواتر کی قید سے خارج ہو جائینگی کیونکہ ان کا نقل اگر چہ بعض مخصوص مصاحف میں ہوا ہے لیکن یہ نقل بطریق احاد ہے جیسے وہ قرآة جو حضرت ابی بن کعبے کے مصحف کے ساتھ مختص ہیں یا ان کا نقل بطریق شہرہ ہے جیسے وہ قرأت جو مختص بمصحف ابن مسعود نہیں بہر حال ان کا نقل بالتواتر نہیں ہے لہذا یہ خارج ہو جائیگی فلاحاجة الى ذكر الانزال الخ اس وقت وصف انزال اور اعجاز کے ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح بلا شبہہ کا لفظ تاکید تواتر کی خاطر ذکر کرنے کی حاجت نہیں کیونکہ ان کے بدون مقصور تعریف یعنی احتراز عن جميع ما عدا القرآن حاصل ہے۔ اما التنمية فالمشهور الخ امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب مشہور جو اکثر کتب متقدمین میں مذکور ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ تسمیہ قرآن مجید کی جز نہیں ہے بجز اس تسمیہ کو جو سورۃ نمل میں ایک آیت کا بعض حصہ ہے۔ انه من سليمان و انه بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم یہ تو قران مجید کا حصہ ہے اور وہ تسمیہ جو اوائل سور میں ہے وہ جزر قرآن نہیں ہے الا ان المتائحرین اور متاخرین کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام کے نزدیک وہ تسمیہ جو اوائل سور میں ہے وہ قرآن مجید کی صرف ایک آیت ہے اور اس کا نزول فصل بین السور کی خاطر ہے ۔ بدليل انها دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ تسمیہ قرآن مجید میں بخط قرآن لکھی گئی ہے اور اس پر سلف میں سے کسی سے بھی انکار اور نکیر منقول نہیں حالانکہ تجرید القرآن عن غیر القرآن کا حکم تاکیدی ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ تسمیہ جزیرہ من القرآن ہے دعدم جواز الصلوة چند مسائل سے تسمیہ کے متعلق عدم قرآنیہ کا شبہ ہوتا تھا یہ ان کا دفع کر رہا ہے ایک مسئلہ یہ کہ نماز میں اگر تسمیہ پر اکتفا کیا جائے تو نماز صحیح نہیں ہوتی حالانکہ امام کے نزدیک فریضہ قراءة کے ادا ہونے کے لئے ایک آیت کافی ہے اس کا جواب دیا انما هو للشبهة الخر يعني عدم جواز الصلاة کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس کے آیت تامہ ہونے میں شبہ ہے یعنی تسمیہ مکمل آیت نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے مقدار فریضہ ادا نہیں ہوگا دوسرا مسئلہ یہ تھا کہ جنب اور حائض کے لئے
Clarifying, he said: The definition of the Quran is that which has been transmitted to us in its entirety. The term 'book' and 'Quran' is used by the usuliyyun (jurisprudents), unlike the theologians for whom 'Quran' applies to the eternal attribute that is uncreated. For the usuliyyun, it applies both to the whole as a whole and to every part that can serve as evidence for a ruling, because they discuss the Book of Allah as evidence for rulings, and each verse serves as evidence, not only the whole. So they needed to seek common attributes between the whole and the parts to use in a definition that applies to both whole and part. For example, being miraculous, being revealed to the Messenger, being written in the mushafs, being transmitted via tawatur—these are attributes common equally to whole and part. Some scholars considered all these attributes in the definition; some only considered revelation and inimitability because these are necessary attributes in every era of the Quran, unlike writing and transmission, as in the time of the Messenger the Quran existed without being written in mushafs or transmitted to us. So these are not necessary and should not be used in the definition. Others considered revelation, writing, and transmission because the purpose of the definition is for those who did not witness revelation or the time of the Messenger, so they know the Quran through transmission and writing in mushafs. In their time, these are inseparable, so they are clearer in indicating the intended meaning. Thus defining with these is beneficial for them, unlike inimitability because it is not clear for them, as knowledge of inimitability is the work of scholars specialized in ma'ani and bayan. And it does not include every part because inimitability is only of a surah or its equivalent, as Allah's saying 'fa'tu bi suratin min mithlihi' indicates. The author sufficed with mentioning 'transmitted in the mushafs' because with it the purpose of definition is achieved and exclusion of everything other than the Quran is obtained, because all other heavenly books, divine hadiths, abrogated recitation verses, and prophetic hadiths are not transmitted between the covers of the mushafs. Because it is a name for this well-known specific collection known to people, even children know it, and all mentioned are not transmitted in this well-known mushaf. And the irregular recitations (qira'at shadhdhah) are excluded by the condition of tawatur because their transmission, even if in some specific mushafs, is via ahad (isolated) or mashhur (well-known), like those specific to Ubayy ibn Ka'b's mushaf or Ibn Mas'ud's, but in any case not by tawatur, so they are excluded. There is no need to mention 'inzal' and 'i'jaz', nor the word 'bila shubhah' for emphasis of tawatur, because without them the intended exclusion is achieved. As for basmalah: the famous madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa, mentioned in most early books, is that the basmalah is not part of the Quran except for the basmalah in Surah al-Naml which is part of a verse. That is part of the Quran. The basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is not part of the Quran. However, according to the later scholars, the correct view is that according to the Imam, the basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is only one verse of the Quran, revealed to separate between surahs. The evidence is that the basmalah is written in the Quran in the script of the Quran, and no rejection or disapproval from the Salaf is transmitted, even though the rule of purifying the Quran from non-Quran is emphasized, so it is known that the basmalah is part of the Quran. Several issues used to create doubt about its Quranicity. One: if one suffices with the basmalah in prayer, the prayer is not valid, even though according to the Imam one verse is sufficient for the obligatory recitation. The answer: it is due to doubt - it is not a complete verse, so the obligatory amount is not fulfilled. Second issue: for the junub and menstruating woman...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of the Quran and the ruling on basmalah. It begins by clarifying that for usul scholars, 'Quran' and 'book' apply both to the entire collection and to each individual verse that serves as evidence for a ruling. This is unlike theologians who take 'Quran' as an eternal attribute. The commentator then explains why the definition must include attributes common to both whole and part, such as being miraculous, revealed, written in mushafs, and transmitted via tawatur. Different scholars prioritize different attributes: some require all, others only revelation and inimitability (since they are necessary at all times), while others include writing and transmission for later generations who rely on these. Inimitability is excluded as a defining attribute for the common people because it is not evident to them. The commentator then explains why the author (al-Musannif) sufficed with mentioning 'transmitted in the mushafs'—it excludes all non-Quranic materials like previous scriptures, hadith qudsi, abrogated verses, etc. The condition of tawatur excludes irregular recitations. The discussion then shifts to basmalah: the famous view of Imam Abu Hanifa (from early books) is that basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is not part of the Quran, except the one in Surah al-Naml. However, later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirin) attribute to Imam Abu Hanifa the view that it is a single verse revealed to separate surahs. They support this by noting its presence in the mushaf and the lack of objection from the Salaf. The commentator then addresses two objections: (1) why is prayer not valid if one recites only the basmalah? Because it is not a complete verse (it is incomplete as a verse? Actually the basis is that it is doubted to be a complete verse, so the obligatory recitation amount is not fulfilled). (2) The ruling for junub and ha'id (impure persons) is cut off but presumably relates to handling the mus'haf.

Key Terms
تسمیة (tasmiyah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'.
متواتر (mutawatir): Transmission by such a large number that collusion on falsehood is impossible, a condition for Quranic authenticity.
معجز (mu'jiz): A miraculous attribute of the Quran, proving its divine origin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of the passage, why did he suffice with 'transmitted in mushafs' in the definition without mentioning 'inzal' and 'i'jaz'?
A) Because inzal and i'jaz are not real attributes of the Quran.
B) Because the definition already excludes all non-Quranic materials using those two conditions.
C) Because the author forgot to include them.
D) Because the definition is meant only for scholars who know inzal and i'jaz.

Key Takeaway
The usuli definition of the Quran must be inclusive of both the whole and each part, and the simplest effective definition uses tawatur and writing in the mushafs.

Al-Quran as Source

The Basmalah: Is It a Verse of the Quran? — The Hanafi Internal Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the Quranic status of the basmalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on the basmalah, state the evidence for each, and evaluate the tarjih (preferred view) of the later scholars.

Core Idea
The basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is a single verse for separation, not part of every surah, according to the later Hanafi view.

This lesson explores the debate within the Hanafi school regarding the Quranic status of the basmalah at the start of surahs. The passage presents the famous view that it is not Quran (except in Surah al-Naml) and the later view that it is a single verse for separation. We examine the evidence and the practical implications for prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Position 1 (mashhur early view): basmalah is not part of the Quran except in Surah al-Naml. Position 2 (later scholars' attribution to Abu Hanifa): it is a single verse revealed to separate surahs.
Note that this is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not between madhhabs.
2
List the evidence for each position
For the first: if one recites only basmalah in prayer, the prayer is invalid because it is not a complete verse, so it cannot fulfill the obligatory recitation. For the second: basmalah is written in the mushaf in Quranic script, and no Salafi objection is recorded against it being part of the Quran.
The writing in the mushaf is a strong indicator, as the Salaf were strict about not mixing non-Quran with Quran.
3
Analyze the prayer invalidity argument
The early view uses the fact that prayer is invalid if only basmalah is recited to argue it is not a complete verse. The later view responds that the invalidity is due to doubt (shubhah) about its completeness, not because it is definitively non-Quran.
This shows how the same fact can be interpreted differently.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
Later scholars prefer the view that basmalah is one verse for separation. They argue that the absence of Salaf objection, combined with its consistent writing in the mushaf, outweighs the prayer invalidity argument, which can be explained by doubt.
This is a clear example of how later Hanafi scholarship refines earlier positions.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if one recites basmalah alone in prayer intending it as Quran, does it fulfill the recitation obligation? According to the early view, no. According to the later view, yes (since it is a verse), but the doubt remains, so caution is recommended.
Knowing this helps muftis give appropriate guidance.
