And some of them made sharing obligatory in conjunction of sentences as well. They even said: By means of conjunction in wording and its correspondence in order, its correspondence in ruling is transmitted. So they said: 'Establish prayer and give zakat.' Here, conjunction of sentences necessitates correspondence in ruling. Since prayer is not obligatory on a minor, therefore zakat is also not obligatory on a minor. In this, both sentences share the same ruling. It seems plausible that according to them, this issue is based on that the addressee of 'establish prayer' is exactly the same addressee of 'give zakat'. Since a minor is not the addressee of 'establish prayer', therefore he is also not the addressee of 'give zakat'. Then we say: The issue according to us Hanafis is that zakat is not obligatory on a minor. But our proof is not the conjunction in wording; rather, our proof is that zakat is not obligatory on a minor because it is pure worship, meaning it has no element of burden and hardship, and a minor is not capable of the obligation of pure worship. And 'ushr and sadaqat al-fitr have a meaning of burden besides worship, so they are obligatory on a minor. And those who assert the obligation of zakat say that the address of prayer and zakat includes minors, but reason excludes minors from the obligation of prayer because it is a physical worship and the minor is exempted due to inability to bear physical hardship. But zakat is financial worship, and his wealth can afford it, so his guardian can pay it on his behalf. And this is invalid according to us: the imposition of sharing in sentences is invalid according to us, because sharing is established only when the second sentence is in need of the first. For example, when he says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free.' Here the slave's freedom will also be suspended on the condition of entering the house because the second clause is in the ruling of a singular word in terms of need, because the original in particles is sharing. And this can be established only when the 'عطف' is on the result, even if this sentence is in itself a nominal sentence. But in the ruling of need, it is like a singular word, so its 'عطف' will be on the result, so that the conjunctive waw remains on its original usage. So the 'عطف' on the 'انت طالق' (the subject) is like 'عبدي حر' also on 'انت طالق', and both will be suspended on the same condition of entering the house, unlike the case where the خبر is repeated. Because here the خبر is made explicit, so it is known that the conjunction is not on 'انت طالق' because otherwise merely 'وضربتك' would suffice; there would be no need to mention 'طالق'. So this second clause is not suspended on the same condition. And the appearance of the خبر here is evidence of non-participation in the result. When he mentioned that sharing is established when the second sentence is in need of the first, an objection arises: In 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free', 'my slave is free' is a complete sentence that is not in need of what precedes it, so it would be appropriate that it not be related to the mentioned condition but rather be an independent statement conjoined to the whole condition and result. So he answered...
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage delves into a usul dispute regarding 'atf al-jumal (conjunction of sentences). Some scholars argue that when two sentences are conjoined by waw, they share the same ruling (hukm). They base this on the Quranic verse 'Establish prayer and give zakat', concluding that since prayer is not obligatory on minors, zakat is also not obligatory. The Hanafi position, however, rejects this reasoning. While agreeing that zakat is not obligatory on minors, Hanafis provide a different rationale: zakat is 'ibada mahda (pure worship) without an element of hardship, and minors are not eligible for such obligations. In contrast, 'ushr and sadaqat al-fitr include a hardship element, so they are obligatory. The passage then critiques the opposing view, stating that the principle of sharing in sentences is invalid unless the second sentence is dependent on the first. It illustrates with the conditional example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free.' Here, even though 'my slave is free' is a complete sentence, it is treated like a singular word in terms of need for the condition, because the waw of conjunction inherently implies sharing. However, if the predicate is repeated (as in 'you are divorced, and divorced'), it indicates that the second clause is not attached to the same condition. The passage ends with an objection and the beginning of an answer.

Key Terms
عطف الجمل (‘aṭf al-jumal): Conjunction of one sentence with another by means of a conjunctive particle (waw)
عبادة محضة (‘ibāda maḥḍa): Pure worship that involves no worldly burden or hardship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider the verse 'أقيموا الصلاة وآتوا الزكاة' insufficient to prove zakat is obligatory on minors?
A) Because the verse is abrogated
B) Because the conjunction does not necessitate sharing in ruling; rather, zakat is 'ibada mahda and minors are exempted
C) Because the verse only addresses adults
D) Because zakat is not mentioned in the verse

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conjunction of sentences does not automatically transfer ruling; the ruling must be independently established.

Analysis of Quranic Verse on Qadhf
Analyzing the conjunction of 'la taqbalū' with 'fajlidū' in the verse on slander

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of conjunction to identify when two Quranic commands are conjoined based on sentence type and addressee.

Core Idea
Two commands conjoined only if both performative and addressed to same authority.

This lesson examines the relationship between the two commands in the qadhf verse of Surah al-Nur. By analyzing sentence type (insha vs khabar) and addressee (judges or general), the Hanafi usul reveals that the prohibition of accepting testimony is not an independent ruling but part of the same hadd penalty. Understanding this conjunction rule is essential for deriving correct rulings from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two commands
Locate 'fajlidū' (scourge) and 'la taqbalū' (do not accept) in the verse. Both are imperative forms.
These are the two main rulings in the qadhf verse.
2
Classify sentence types
Determine if each is insha'iyyah (performative) or khabariyyah (declarative). Both are imperatives, hence insha.
Insha brings about a ruling; khabar reports a fact.
3
Identify the addressee
Who is being commanded? Verses of hudud typically address the ruler/judge. Both commands are directed to the imams.
Not all Quranic addresses are general; some are specific to authorities.
4
Apply the conjunction rule
Only similar sentences with the same addressee can be conjoined by the waw. Since both are insha and addressed to imams, 'la taqbalū' is conjoined to 'fajlidū'.
The waw here is 'atf (conjunction), not isti'naf (new sentence).
5
Derive the thamarah
The benefit: both commands constitute the complete hadd for qadhf. The prohibition of testimony is part of the punishment, not a standalone rule.
This affects whether the ban on testimony is mandatory or discretionary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وھذا جعلنا قولہ تعالیٰ ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا حاصل یہ کہ لا تقبلوا جملہ انشائیہ ہے۔ اور اس کے ساتھ خطاب ائمہ کو ہے جیسے فاجلدوا انشائیہ ہے اور مخاطب اس کے ساتھ ائمہ ہیں۔ اسی مناسبت کی وجہ سے لا تقبلوا کا عطف جزا یعنی فاجلدوا پر ہوگا اور یہ دونوں امر حد قذف میں درج ہوں گے اور بخلاف اولئک ھم الفاسقون یہ جملہ خبریہ ہے اور اس کے ساتھ ائمہ مخاطب نہیں ہیں لہذا اس کا عطف جزا پر نہیں ہوگا ۔ وثمرہ ہذا نانی فی آخر فصل الاستثنا انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ ۔
And this is why we consider the statement of Allah 'And never accept their testimony [wa la taqbalū lahum shahādatan]' (24:4). The summary is that 'la taqbalū' is a performative (insha'iyyah) sentence, and it addresses the imams (judges), just as 'fajlidū' (scourge them) is performative and addressed to the imams. Due to this suitability, 'la taqbalū' is conjoined to the result, i.e., 'fajlidū', and both commands will be included in the hadd of qadhf. As opposed to 'ulā'ika hum al-fāsiqūn' (they are the transgressors), which is a declarative (khabariyyah) sentence and does not address the imams, therefore it is not conjoined to the result. And the benefit of this will appear at the end of the chapter on exception, God willing.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Quranic verse on qadhf (false accusation of adultery), specifically the relationship between the two commands: 'fajlidūhum' (scourge them) and 'wa lā taqbalū lahum shahādatan abadan' (never accept their testimony). The author argues that the second command is conjoined (ma'tūf) to the first because both are performative (inshā'iyyah) sentences addressed to the same audience (the imams/judges). This is a rule of conjunction: only sentences of the same type and addressing the same audience can be conjoined. In contrast, the phrase 'ulā'ika hum al-fāsiqūn' is declarative (khabariyyah) and not addressed to the judges, so it cannot be conjoined. The fruit of this analysis is that both rulings are part of the full hadd penalty for qadhf. This shows the importance of matching sentence type and audience in usul al-fiqh for interpreting Quranic injunctions correctly.

Key Terms
انشائیہ (inshā'iyyah): A performative sentence that brings about a ruling or effect, such as an imperative or prohibition.
خبریہ (khabariyyah): A declarative sentence that can be true or false.
عطف ('atf): Conjunction of one element to another, here with the particle 'waw'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because both are declarative sentences.
B) Because both are performative and addressed to the same audience.
C) Because the verse is about qadhf.
D) Because the waw of conjunction always joins sentences.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of accepting testimony in the qadhf verse is conjoined to the lashing command, forming one complete hadd penalty.

The Particle Fa Entering upon the 'Illah: Final Causality in Hanafi Usul
Explains the rationale for fa entering upon a cause using final causality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the particle fa can enter upon a cause in the context of final causality, and apply this understanding to interpret Quranic and poetic examples.

Core Idea
Fa enters upon a cause only when the cause is viewed as an effect of its final purpose.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the particle fa typically indicates immediate succession (ta'qib). However, it can grammatically enter upon a cause (illah) when that cause is considered from the perspective of final causality (illa ghā'iyya). In such cases, the cause is actually an effect (ma'lul) of the intended purpose, and fa's entry respects its original meaning. This lesson unpacks that reasoning with two examples: a Quranic verse and a line of poetry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of fa
Recall that fa in Arabic usually indicates immediate succession (تعقيب) — the second event follows the first without delay. This is the default meaning.
2
Understand the problem: fa entering upon a cause
If fa enters upon a cause (illah), it would seem to imply the effect follows the cause immediately. But in reality, the cause precedes its effect, so fa would appear to reverse the order. The Hanafi solution is to view the cause as an effect of the final purpose.
3
Analyze the final cause (illa ghā'iyya) relationship
The final cause is the purpose or intended goal. In mental existence, it is a cause for the agent's action, but in external existence, it is an effect (the action produces the goal). Thus, when the 'illah in the text is actually the final purpose, it is considered ma'lul (effect) of the intended action, making fa's entry appropriate.
Example: 'Take provisions, for the best provision is taqwa.' The command to take provisions is the intended purpose, so it becomes the final cause of 'best provision is taqwa' — the latter is the ma'lul of that purpose.
4
Apply to the Quranic verse
In 'وتزودوا فإن خير الزاد التقوى', the intended purpose is 'tazawwadu' (take provisions). This purpose is the final cause for 'khayr al-zad al-taqwa' (the best provision is taqwa). Thus, fa enters upon 'khayr al-zad' not as a cause in the usual sense, but as the ma'lul (effect) of the intended command.
The legal implication: the verse encourages taking provisions, not relying on begging.
5
Consider the alternative explanation
Alternatively, fa enters upon the 'illah when the 'illah has continuity (dawām), making it delayed from the initial ruling, so it is suitable for fa to indicate subsequent entry. This shows the nuance of Hanafi linguistic analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تھا اس لئے اس کی توجیہ کر رہا ہے کہ علیہ پر اس وقت داخل ہوگی جب علہ سے مقصد معاون ہو تو علہ کے لئے یہ معلول علتہ غائیہ ہو جائے گا فیصير العلة معلولا تو اس وقت میں علم معلول کے درجہ میں ہو جائے گی اور معلول جو علہ غانیہ تھا یہ درجہ علہ میں ہو جائے گا اصل یہ ہے کہ علیہ عائیہ باعتبار وجود ذہنی کے فاعلیتہ فاعل کے لئے علہ ہوتی ہے لیکن باعتبار وجود خارجی کے معلول ہوتی ہے فقدا تاک الغوث میں نا داخل علی العلہ ہے لیکن چونکہ اس سے مقصود اصلی ابشار ہے لہذا وہ علہ غائیہ کے درجہ میں ہو کر اتاک الغوث کے لئے علت ہوگا اور اتاک الغوت معلول کے درجہ میں ہوگا اس لئے اس پر فاداخل ہوتی ہے ۔ فلهذا تدخل على العلة یعنی اس وقت فا کا دخول علی العلة باعتبار اس کے نہ ہوا کہ وہ علہ ہے بلکہ باعتبار اس کے معلول ہونے کے ہوا تو دخول فا تعقیبہ صحیح ہوگا ومن ذلك قوله تعالى وتزودوا فإن خير الزاد التقوى یعنی جب سفر حج کرو تو اپنے ساتھ زاد راہ لے جایا کرو کیونکہ اس کی بھلائی تقوی ہے یعنی سوال اور گداگری سے بچ جاؤ گے تو خیر الزاد التقوى کہنے سے مقصود بالذات یہ ہے کہ یہ لوگ اپنے ساتھ زاد راہ لے جائیں یہ نہ ہو کہ متوکل علی اللہ بن کر نکالیں پھر حرم میں پہونچ کر لوگوں سے سوال کرتے پھریں تو جب تزودوا مقصود بالذات ہوا تو یہ خیر الزاد کی علت غنائیہ ہو جائے گا اور خیر الزاد بدرجہ معلول اس لئے اس پر فاداخل ہوتی ہے وقول الشاعر اذا ملك لم یکن ذاهبة یعنی جب بادشاہ صاحب حبہ نہ ہو یعنی لوگوں پر ہیہ اور عطیہ نہ کرے تو فدعه فدولته ذاهبة پس اسے چھوڑ دے کہ اس کی دولت وسلطنت جانیوالی اور ضائع ہونیوالی ہے یعنی اس شعر سے مقصود بالذات یہی بتلانا ہے کہ جب وہ شخص صاحب ہیہ نہ ہو تو یہ علہ غانیہ کے درجہ میں ہو جائے گی۔ اور دولتہ ذاهبہ بدرجہ معلول تو فا اس لئے اس پر داخل ہوئی ہے ۔ یا اس کی توجیہ یوں بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ فاعلل پر اس وقت داخل ہوئی جب علل کو دوام حاصل ہو تو اس وقت یہ ابتدائے حکم سے متراخی ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے نام تعقیبی ان پر داخل ہو جاتی ہے
He is explaining that fa enters upon the 'illah when the purpose is concurrent with the 'illah, then for the 'illah this becomes a ma'lul as the final cause (علة غائية), so the 'illah becomes ma'lul. Then knowledge becomes in the rank of ma'lul, and the ma'lul which was the final cause becomes in the rank of 'illah. The principle is that the final cause (علة غائية) in terms of mental existence is a cause for the agent's action, but in terms of external existence it is an effect (ma'lul). For example, in 'fa'atāka al-ghaythu' (then the rain came), fa enters upon the 'illah, but because the intended purpose is relief, it becomes like a final cause and becomes a cause for 'atāka al-ghaythu', and 'atāka al-ghaythu' becomes the ma'lul. Therefore, fa enters upon it. So this is why fa enters upon the 'illah: it is not because it is a cause, but because it is considered as a ma'lul, so the entry of fa for immediate succession is correct. And from that is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And take provisions, for indeed the best provision is taqwā.' That is, when you travel for Hajj, take provisions with you, because its goodness is taqwā, meaning you will avoid begging. So the intended meaning of 'the best provision is taqwā' is that these people take provisions with them, not that they go out trusting Allah and then beg. So when 'take provisions' is the intended purpose, it becomes the final cause of 'the best provision', and 'the best provision' is in the rank of ma'lul. Therefore, fa enters upon it. And the poet's saying: 'When a king is not generous, then leave him, for his kingdom is disappearing.' Meaning when a king is not generous and does not give gifts, then leave him, for his state and sovereignty are passing and wasting away. The intended meaning of this verse is to inform that when the person is not generous, this becomes like a final cause, and 'his kingdom is disappearing' is in the rank of ma'lul. So fa entered upon it. Or it can be explained alternatively: that fa enters upon the 'illah when the 'illah has continuity; then it becomes delayed from the beginning of the ruling, so it is suitable for fa to enter upon it as a subsequent thing.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a rule about the usage of the particle fa (ف) in legal language. It explains that although fa typically indicates immediate succession (تعقيب), it can grammatically and logically enter upon a cause (علة) when that cause is considered from the perspective of final causality. In the chain of purpose, the cause becomes an effect (معلول) of the intended goal, and thus fa's entry upon it is appropriate. The author provides two proofs: first from the Qur'anic verse 'وتزودوا فإن خير الزاد التقوى' where the command to take provisions (تزودوا) is the intended purpose, making it the final cause, and 'خير الزاد التقوى' the effect, so fa connects them with immediate succession. Second, a poetic example illustrates the same. An alternative explanation is also offered: fa enters upon the 'illah when the 'illah is continuous (دائم), causing the fa to indicate delay from the initial ruling rather than immediate succession from the start. This nuanced discussion shows how Hanafi usul al-fiqh analyzes particles for precise legal inference.

Key Terms
ف (fa): A particle (حرف) that usually indicates immediate succession (تعقيب) but can grammatically enter upon a cause when the cause is viewed as an effect of its final purpose.
علة غائية (ʿilla ghāʾiyya): A final cause or purpose; an intended goal that, in terms of external existence, becomes an effect but in terms of mental conception is a cause.
تعقيب (taʿqīb): Immediate succession; the meaning typically associated with fa, indicating that one event follows another without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because fa changes its meaning when used with a cause.
B) Because the cause is considered as an effect (ma'lul) of the final purpose, making it suitable for fa's indication of succession.
C) Because fa indicates delay, not succession, when used with causes.
D) Because the cause is always a grammatical object.

Key Takeaway
Fa enters upon a cause only when that cause is considered as an effect of the final purpose, preserving the meaning of immediate succession.

The Meaning of 'Aw' in Highway Robbery Punishments: Takhyir or Tafsir?
Analyzing the Quranic verse on punishments for highway robbers to determine the meaning of 'aw'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that 'aw' can indicate tafsir (division) rather than takhyir (choice) when the context links punishments to specific crimes.

Core Idea
In the Qur'anic verse on highway robbery, 'aw' divides punishments by crime type, not grants a choice.

This passage examines the Qur'anic verse prescribing punishments for highway robbers (qat' al-tariq) and the meaning of the particle 'aw' (or) in it. While a literal reading might suggest that the imam can choose any punishment, the Hanafi school argues that the context demands a division (tafsir): each punishment corresponds to a specific type of crime. Understanding this usul principle helps you see how the Hanafi school derives rulings from the Qur'an with attention to customary practice (urf) and internal consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and the contested word
Locate the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33) in the passage. Notice the four punishments listed with the particle 'aw' (or) between them. This particle is the focus of the dispute.
The verse mentions execution, crucifixion, amputation of opposite hand and foot, and exile.
2
State the opposing view (takhyir)
Some scholars argue that 'aw' in a declaratory (insha'i) context gives choice. Therefore, the imam may select any punishment for any highway robber.
This view is presented and then rebutted in the passage.
3
Present the Hanafi view and its proof
The Hanafi position is that 'aw' indicates tafsir (division). The proof is based on the context: the punishments are juxtaposed with the types of crimes, and custom (urf) shows that greater crimes warrant greater punishments. If 'aw' meant takhyir, a lesser punishment could be applied to a greater crime, which is unreasonable.
The passage lists four crime types: (1) only murder, (2) murder + theft, (3) only theft, (4) only intimidation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that the verse is a division (taqsim) of punishments according to crime types. The word 'aw' here functions to separate distinct cases, not to provide a choice. The practical consequence of takhyir would lead to disproportion.
The author cites hadith from Ibn Abbas to support the division.
5
Note the practical implication (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, the imam must apply the specific punishment for each specific crime. Under the opposing view, the imam could choose any punishment regardless of the crime. This difference affects actual sentencing.
For example, a robber who only kills must be executed, not just exiled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اندر چاہیے واقع کر سکتا ہے اور یہ ایقاع انشاء عشق ہے ومن حيث انه اخبار لغت اور بائیں حیثیت کہ لغیرہ یہ اخبار ہے لہذا موجب شک ہے اور اخبار بالمجہول ہے یہ معلوم نہیں کہ ان عیدین میں سے کون آزاد ہے۔ فعليه ان يظهر آن پس اس پر لازم ہے کہ ما فی الواقع یعنی جو نفس الامر میں آزاد ہے اس کا اظہار کرے یہ اظہار انشاء نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ ماعوفی الواقع کا بیان اور اظہار ہے فلما كان للبیان بیان یعنی تعیین احدھما کہ متعین کرنا کہ ان میں سے فلاں آزاد ہے اس کو دو قسم کے شہر حاصل ہیں ایک شیر انشاء کا دوسرا شبہ اخبار کا عملنا بالشبعین ہم نے دونوں شھوں پر عمل کیا بلحاظ شبہ انشاء کے شرطنا صلاحية المحل کہ محل صلاحیتہ عتق رکھتا ہوتا کہ اس میں انشاء عشق ہو سکے اور یہ صلاحیت بوقت بیان کے ضروری ہے حتی ازامات احمد مما یعنی جب عبدین کو کہا ہذا حر او ہذا اس کے بعد ایک غلام مر گیا اب وہ کہتا کہ ان دوئیں سے میری مراد یہی میت تھا تو اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی کیونکہ بوقت بیان کے میت صلاحیہ عشق نہیں رکھتا ۔ ومن حيث انه اخبار اور بائیں حیثیت کہ اس کے اندر شبہ اخبار ہے يجبر على البیان تو بیان کرنے کے لئے اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا کہ وہ واضح کرے کہ کو نسا غلام آزاد ہے نانه لا جبر في الانشات انتا میں جبر نہیں ہوتا بخلاف الاخبار بخلاف اخبار کے کہ اس کے اندر جی علی البیان کیا جاتا ہے ۔ کہا اذا اقر بالجھول جیسے کسی کے حق میں مجہول شی کا اقرار کرتا ہے مثلا یوں کہتا ہے کہ فلاں شخص کی میرے اوپر کوئی شتی واجب ہے تو اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا کہ بیان کرے کہ وہ کیا شتی ہے۔ اور اس اقرار میں ایسی شئی بیان کرے جس کی بازار میں قیمت ہو - هذا ما قیل یہی مراد ہے اس قول کی جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ بیان من وجہ انشا ہوتا ہے اور من وجہ اخبار یعنی اس کے اندر دونوں قسم کے شبھین موجود ہیں ۔ وفي قوله وكلت هذا وهذا اس صورت میں اگر چہ توکیل مھم ہے کیونکہ او احد الشینین لا على التعيين کے لئے آتا ہے لہذا قیا سا تو جائز نہیں ہے لیکن استحسانا جائز ہے کیونکہ مبنی وکالتہ علی التوسع ہے اور یہ جہالہ مفضى الى المنازعہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ مقصود ایک شئی کا بیچنا ہے اب جو بھی فروخت کر دے گا جائے ہے لہذا کہا۔ ایھما تصرف جاز جو بھی تصرف کرے جائے ہے پھر دوسرے کو اختیار تصرف نہیں رہیگا۔ اگر چہ وہی شئی موکل کے پاس بطور مصیبہ یا ارث کے واپس آگئی ہے تب بھی دوسرا فروخت نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ جو مقصود من التوکیل تھا ایک مرتبہ حاصل ہو چکا ہے اور توکیل ختم ہو چکی ہے۔ فلهذا اى لما قلنا ان اولی الانشاء للتغيير یعنی جو ہم نے کہا کہ لفظ او انشار میں برائے تخیر ہوتا ہے اسی بنا پر اوجب البعض التخيير بعض حضرات نے قطع الطریق کے تمام اقسام میں تخیر کو ثابت قرار دیا ہے یعنی امام وقت کو اختیار ہے کہ جس قسم کی قطع الطریق ہو جو سزا امام چاہے دے سکتا ہے بقولہ تعالٰی اللہ تعالی نے قاطع الطریق کی سزا بیان فرمائی بقولہ ان یقتلوا او يصبوا او تقطع ايديهم وارجلهم من خلاف او ينفوا یہ چار قسم کی سزائیں ہیں اور ان میں لفظ او استعمال ہوا ہے اور یہ استعمال سے بھی انشاء ہیں لہذا برائے تخیر ہو گا لہذا امام وقت کو اختیار جو سزا چاہے دے سکتا ہے۔
قلنا ہم اس کے جواب میں کہتے ہیں کہ ذکر الاجزیه ان مختلف مزاول كا ذكر مقابلة لانواع الجناية بمقابلہ اقسام جنایتہ کے ہے یعنی قاطع الطریق سے مختلف اقسام کی جنایات ہوتی ہیں لہذا ایک ایک سزا بمقابلہ ایک ایک جنایتہ کے ہے کیونکہ ازدیاد جنایت کے ساتھ سزا نہ یادہ ہو جاتی ہے اگر جنایہ کم درجہ کی ہو تو سزا بھی کم درجہ کی ہوگی ۔ جزا سینہ سینہ مثلما لہذا تقسیم اجزہ یہ علی اقسام الجنایہ ہے او برائے تخیر نہیں ورنہ تو کہیں زیادہ جنایت پر ناقص سزا اور بالعکس لازم آجائے گا جو صحیح نہیں ہے وهی معلومة عادة اور یہ انواع جنایۃ عادہ معلوم ہیں جس کی مصنف نے یوں تفصیل فرمائی من قتل یعنی قاطع الطریق نے صرف قتل کیا اور مال نہیں لوٹا اوقتل واخد مال یعنی قتل بھی کیا اور مال بھی لوٹا اواخد مال صرف مال لوٹا قتل نہیں کیا او تخولیف صرف ڈرایا دھمکایا نہ قتل کیا نہ مال لوٹا ۔ اس کے بعد مصنف نے سزاؤں کی تفصیل علی سبیل اللف والنشر المرتب کی نالقتل جزاه القتل یعنی جب قاطع الطریق نے صرف قتل نفس کیا تو اس کی سزا صرف یہی ہے کہ قاطع الطریق کو قتل کر دیا جائیگا والقتل والاخذ قاطع نے قتل بھی کیا اور مال بھی لوٹا تو جزاؤه الصلب جزا اس کی یہ ہے کہ قاطع الطریق کو صلیب پر لٹکا کر سزائے موت دی جائے واخذ المال جب قاطع نے صرف مال لوٹا اور قتل نہیں کیا تو جزاؤه قطع اليد والرجل ہاتھ اور پاؤں من خلاف کاٹ لیا جائے یعنی دایاں ہاتھ اور بایاں پاؤں والتخويف جب قاطع الطریق نے صرف تخویف کی اور نہ قتل کیا نہ مال لوٹا تو جزاه النفی اسی الحبس الدائم جب ایک جماعت قاطعین آن انواع جنایتہ میں سے جس قسم کی جنایت کریں ان تمام پر وہی سزا جاری کی جائے گی جو اس جنایت کے مقابلہ میں ہے یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ ہر فرد پردہ سزا جاری کریں جس قسم کی جنایت اس نے کی مثلاً ایک جماعت نے قطع الطریق کیا بعض نے قتل کیا بعض نے مال لوٹا بعض نے ڈرایا دھمکایا تو تمام پر صلیب وارد ہو گا یہ نہیں کہ قاتل پر قتل آخذ مال پر قطع اور تحریف پر جبس یوں تقسیم نہیں ہوگی بلکہ تمام کے تمام اس صورت میں تحقی صلیب میں علی انه ورد في الحديث الخ یعنی حدیث شریف میں ان سزاؤں کی تبین دبیان اسی مثال اور طریق پر بیان ہوئی ہے جیسے انکی تفصیل کی گئی ہے اور یہ روایت از ابن عباس مروی ہے جس کو صاحب التلویح نے تلویح میں ذکر کر دیا ہے فلینظر۔ دان اخذ وقتل فعند ابي حنيفة
It can occur within [the statement] and this occurrence is a declaration of love? And from the perspective that it is a report (ikhbar) of language, and on the other hand it is a report (ikhbar) regarding other than itself, therefore it entails doubt (shakk) and it is a report of the unknown; it is not known which of the two slaves is free. Therefore he is required to make it apparent, i.e., to reveal what is in reality (the one who is free in actual fact). This revelation is not a declaration (insha) but rather a statement and expression of what is in reality. Since it is for expression (bayan), i.e., specifying one of them that such-and-such is free, he has two aspects of doubt: one is the doubt of declaration (insha) and the other is the doubt of report (ikhbar). We acted on both doubts: with respect to the doubt of declaration, we condition the suitability of the locus (mahall), i.e., the locus must possess the capacity for emancipation (ittiq) such that a declaration of freedom can occur, and this capacity is necessary at the time of expression, as in the case of Ahmad etc. — when he said to two slaves 'This one is free or this one' and then one slave died, and he says 'I intended this deceased one', his statement is not accepted because at the time of expression the deceased did not possess the capacity for emancipation. And from the perspective that there is a doubt of report (ikhbar) in it, he is compelled to make it clear (yujbar 'ala al-bayan), i.e., he will be forced to clarify which slave is free, because there is no compulsion (jabr) in declarations (insha'at), unlike reports (ikhbar) where compulsion to clarify is applied. It is said: 'When he confesses to something unknown (ijhar bi'l-majhul),' like confessing an unknown thing to someone's right, e.g., he says 'So-and-so has some thing due on me,' then he will be compelled to explain what that thing is; and in that confession he should mention something that has a market price. This is what is meant by the saying that 'bayan (explanation) is in one respect a declaration (insha') and in another respect a report (ikhbar)', i.e., both types of doubt exist in it. And in his statement: 'I deputed this one and this one (wakaltu hadha wa hadha)', in this case, although deputation (tawkīl) is ambiguous because 'aw (or) is used for one of the two things without specification, therefore by analogy (qiyas) it is not permissible, but by istihsan (juristic preference) it is permissible because deputation is based on expansion (tawassu'), and this ambiguity (jahala) does not lead to dispute (munaza'a), because the purpose is to sell one thing; now whichever he sells is permissible. Therefore it is said: 'Whichever one he transacts (tasarrafa) is valid.' Then the other will no longer have the authority to transact, even if the same thing returns to the principal (muwakkil) by way of a gift (hiba) or inheritance, the other cannot sell it because the purpose of deputation has been achieved once and the deputation has ended. For this reason, i.e., because we said that 'aw' in declarations (insha') is for choice (takhyir), on this basis some have affirmed takhyir (choice) in all types of highway robbery (qat' al-tariq), i.e., the imam has the option to impose whichever punishment he wants for whichever type of highway robbery, according to Allah's statement. Allah Most High stated the punishment for the highway robber in His saying: 'that they be killed, or crucified, or have their hands and feet cut off on opposite sides, or be exiled from the land' — these are four types of punishment, and the word 'aw' is used in them, and these punishments are also declarations (insha') from usage, therefore 'aw' indicates choice (takhyir). Therefore the imam has the option to impose whichever punishment he wishes. We say in response: The mention of different punishments (ajziya) is in contrast to the types of crimes (anwa' al-jinaya), i.e., different types of crimes occur from the highway robber, so each punishment is in correspondence to each crime, because the punishment increases with the increase of the crime; if the crime is of a lower degree, the punishment will also be of a lower degree. Each punishment is commensurate (musawiya) with its like; therefore the division of punishments (taqsim al-ajziya) is according to the types of crimes, not for choice (takhyir). Otherwise, a lesser punishment would necessarily apply to a greater crime and vice versa, which is not correct. And these types of crimes are known by custom (mu'ada). The author (musannif) has detailed them as follows: 'Man qatala' — i.e., the highway robber only killed and did not take property; 'wa qatala wa akhadha mal' — i.e., he killed and also took property; 'wa akhadha mal' — i.e., he only took property without killing; 'wa takhwif' — i.e., he only frightened (intimidated) without killing or taking property. After that, the author detailed the punishments according to the method of laf wa nashr murattab (enveloping and spreading in order): 'Fa'l-qatlu jazauh al-qatl' — i.e., when the highway robber only kills a person, his punishment is only that he be killed; 'wa'l-qatlu wa'l-akhdh' — the robber killed and also took property, his punishment is crucifixion (salb); 'wa akhdh al-mal' — when the robber only took property and did not kill, his punishment is cutting of the hand and foot from opposite sides (qat' al-yad wa al-rijl min khilaf), i.e., the right hand and left foot; 'wa al-takhwif' — when the robber only intimidated without killing or taking property, his punishment is exile (nafy) which is permanent imprisonment. When a group of highway robbers commit a certain type of crime from these types, the same punishment will be applied to all of them that corresponds to that crime. It is not meant that each individual is given the punishment corresponding to his own crime; for example, a group committed highway robbery, some killed, some took property, some intimidated, then all will be subject to crucifixion (salb). It is not that the killer is killed, the taker of property has his hand cut, and the intimidator is imprisoned — this division will not happen. Rather, all of them in such a case are [liable to] crucifixion, according to what is reported in the hadith: the clarification of these punishments has come in the noble hadith in the same manner and way as detailed, and this narration is from Ibn Abbas, which the author of al-Talwih has mentioned in al-Talwih, so let him look. Dan akhadha wa qatala fa 'inda Abi Hanifah
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul analysis of the particle 'aw' (or) in the context of the punishments for highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) as stated in the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33). The commentary first discusses a general principle: when someone says 'This slave is free or that slave is free,' the statement has two aspects – it is both a declaration (insha) of freedom and a report (ikhbar) about the reality. Due to this duality, certain rules apply: the capacity of the slave at the time of expression matters, and the speaker can be compelled to clarify which one he actually intended, as in an unknown confession. The author then applies this to the verse on highway robbery, where the four punishments (execution, crucifixion, amputation, exile) are listed with 'aw'. Some scholars argue that 'aw' here indicates takhyir (choice) – the imam may freely choose any punishment for any robber. The Hanafi response is that 'aw' is for tafsir (division): each punishment corresponds to a specific type of crime. The author lists the four crime types (only murder, murder+theft, only theft, only intimidation) and the corresponding punishments (execution, crucifixion, amputation, exile). If a group commits multiple crimes, all members receive the most severe punishment (crucifixion) as per the hadith from Ibn Abbas. The passage ends with the beginning of Abu Hanifa's view on the case of killing and theft, which is not fully given here. The key takeaway for the student: in Hanafi usul, 'aw' does not always mean choice; context and customary practice (urf) determine that it often serves to separate distinct rulings for distinct cases.

Key Terms
او (aw): The particle 'or' used in legal texts. In this passage, it is analyzed as indicating either takhyir (choice) or tafsir (division).
تقسيط (taqsim): Division of punishments according to the types of crimes, as opposed to free choice.
قطع الطريق (qat' al-tariq): Highway robbery, a crime involving armed robbery on the road. Its punishments are prescribed in the Quran.
تخيير (takhyir): Choice; the idea that the imam may freely select any of the listed punishments.
تفسير (tafsir): Division or specification; each punishment applies to a specific case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what does the word 'aw' (or) signify in the Quranic verse on punishments for highway robbery?
A) Takhyir (choice) – the imam may freely select any punishment
B) Tafsir (division) – each punishment corresponds to a specific type of crime
C) Takhsis (specification) – it restricts a general rule
D) Nasikh (abrogation) – it supersedes earlier laws

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in legal texts can signify tafsir (division) when the context pairs options with distinct cases, avoiding arbitrary choice.

The Meaning of 'Aw' in Quran 5:33: Choice or Correspondence?
Explaining the four punishments for highway robbers and the linguistic interpretation of 'aw' in Quran 5:33.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of 'aw' in Quran 5:33 as indicating correspondence rather than free choice, and apply this to the categorization of punishments for highway robbery.

Core Idea
The word 'aw' in legal texts does not always mean 'or' as choice; in Quran 5:33 it distributes each punishment to its specific crime.

This lesson examines the linguistic and legal analysis of the verse on highway robbery (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33). The passage from the sharh explains why the particle 'aw' should not be read as giving a free choice to the ruler, but rather as matching each punishment to a particular category of crime. We will explore the four categories, their corresponding punishments, and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, including Abu Hanifa's nuanced view on combining punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic issue
The verse uses 'aw' between four punishments. The initial apparent meaning is that the ruler may choose any of the four. But the author argues against this.
2
Understand the argument for correspondence
The punishments are mentioned in correspondence to categories of crimes, each crime has a specific punishment. The crime categories are detailed: killing only, killing and taking property, taking property only, intimidation.
3
Analyze the consequences of reading 'aw' as choice
If it were free choice, then for a minor crime a severe punishment could be given, which is unjust. The author uses a qiyas of proportionality.
4
Examine the special case of killing and taking property
Although the verse specifies crucifixion for this combination, Abu Hanifa allows all four punishments because the act can be seen as either one or two crimes. This is based on the hadith of the Urayniyyin.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The Hanafi approach to 'aw' in legal texts: context and qarina (indication) determine whether it indicates takhyir (choice) or tafsil (distribution). Here, the qarina is the mention of different crimes.

ورنہ تو کہیں زیادہ جنایت پر ناقص سزا اور بالعکس لازم آجائے گا جو صحیح نہیں ہے وهی معلومة عادة اور یہ انواع جنایۃ عادہ معلوم ہیں جس کی مصنف نے یوں تفصیل فرمائی من قتل یعنی قاطع الطریق نے صرف قتل کیا اور مال نہیں لوٹا اوقتل واخد مال یعنی قتل بھی کیا اور مال بھی لوٹا اواخد مال صرف مال لوٹا قتل نہیں کیا او تخولیف صرف ڈرایا دھمکایا نہ قتل کیا نہ مال لوٹا ۔ اس کے بعد مصنف نے سزاؤں کی تفصیل علی سبیل اللف والنشر المرتب کی نالقتل جزاه القتل یعنی جب قاطع الطریق نے صرف قتل نفس کیا تو اس کی سزا صرف یہی ہے کہ قاطع الطریق کو قتل کر دیا جائیگا والقتل والاخذ قاطع نے قتل بھی کیا اور مال بھی لوٹا تو جزاؤه الصلب جزا اس کی یہ ہے کہ قاطع الطریق کو صلیب پر لٹکا کر سزائے موت دی جائے واخذ المال جب قاطع نے صرف مال لوٹا اور قتل نہیں کیا تو جزاؤه قطع اليد والرجل ہاتھ اور پاؤں من خلاف کاٹ لیا جائے یعنی دایاں ہاتھ اور بایاں پاؤں والتخويف جب قاطع الطریق نے صرف تخویف کی اور نہ قتل کیا نہ مال لوٹا تو جزاه النفی اسی الحبس الدائم جب ایک جماعت قاطعین آن انواع جنایتہ میں سے جس قسم کی جنایت کریں ان تمام پر وہی سزا جاری کی جائے گی جو اس جنایت کے مقابلہ میں ہے یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ ہر فرد پردہ سزا جاری کریں جس قسم کی جنایت اس نے کی مثلاً ایک جماعت نے قطع الطریق کیا بعض نے قتل کیا بعض نے مال لوٹا بعض نے ڈرایا دھمکایا تو تمام پر صلیب وارد ہو گا یہ نہیں کہ قاتل پر قتل آخذ مال پر قطع اور تحریف پر جبس یوں تقسیم نہیں ہوگی بلکہ تمام کے تمام اس صورت میں تحقی صلیب میں علی انه ورد في الحديث الخ یعنی حدیث شریف میں ان سزاؤں کی تبین دبیان اسی مثال اور طریق پر بیان ہوئی ہے جیسے انکی تفصیل کی گئی ہے اور یہ روایت از ابن عباس مروی ہے جس کو صاحب التلویح نے تلویح میں ذکر کر دیا ہے فلینظر۔ دان اخذ وقتل فعند ابي حنيفة " یعنی جب قاطع الطریق قتل بھی کرتا ہے اور مال بھی لوٹتا ہے تو اس صورت میں جزاؤه الصلیب تھی تو امام ابو حنیفہ نے صلیب کو اسی حالت سے مختص قرار دیا کہ صلیب کی سزا اس جنایتہ کے علاوہ دوسرے قسم میں نہیں آسکتی اور اس حالت جنایۃ کو صلیب کے ساتھ مختص نہیں کیا بلکہ اس حالت میں چار قسم کی سزاؤں کو جائز قرار دیا جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے ۔ ان شاء قطع ثم قتل یعنی قد ید ورجل من خلاف کر کے پھر قتل کر دیا جائے او صلب یعنی قطع کے بعد صلیب کے ذریعہ سزائے موت دے د انشاء قتل یعنی صرف قتل کی سزا دے او صلب یا صرف صلیب کے ذریعہ سے سزائے موت دے۔ لان الجناية يحتمل الاتحاد والتعد و کیونکہ یہ جنابیہ محتمل اتحاد ہے یعنی بایں حیثیت یہ قطع المارہ ہے یعنی گزرنے والوں پر قطع الطریق کی گئی ہے تو اس لحاظ سے یہ ایک جنایہ ہے لہذا ایک مزا یعنی قتل یا صلب پر اکتفا کیا جا سکتا ہے اور اس جنایت کے اندرا احتمال تعدد بھی ہے کیونکہ قاطع نے ایک تو اخذ مال کیا ہے قطع ہے اور دوسرا اس نے قتل کیا ہے جو سبب قتل ہے لہذا ان سببین کا حکم لازم کیا جا سکتا ہے ۔ لہذا قطع اور قتل یا قطع اور صلب ہو سکتا ہے جیسے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے عرنیین کے ساتھ کیا تھا کہ قطع کیا اور حرہ میں ڈالکر سزائے موت دی ۔
Allah Almighty has prescribed the punishment for the highway robber in His saying: 'Indeed, the penalty for those who wage war against Allah and His Messenger and strive upon the earth [to cause] corruption is only that they be killed or crucified or that their hands and feet be cut off from opposite sides or that they be exiled.' These are four types of punishments, and in them the word 'aw' is used, and these [punishments] are also injunctions (insha') from the usage, so it is for choice (takhayyur). Therefore, the Imam has the option to give whichever punishment he wishes. We say in response: The mention of these punishments is a mention in correspondence to the categories of crimes. That is, from the highway robber, different categories of crimes occur. Therefore, each punishment corresponds to each crime, because as the crime increases, the punishment increases. If the crime is of a low degree, then the punishment will also be of a low degree. Punishment is proportionate, so the division of punishments is according to the categories of crimes, not for choice. Otherwise, it would necessitate a deficient punishment for a greater crime and vice versa, which is not correct. And these types of crimes are known by custom. The author has detailed them as follows: 'Man qatala' – the robber only killed and did not take property; 'wa qatala wa akhadha mala' – he killed and also took property; 'wa akhadha mala' – only took property, did not kill; 'wa takhwif' – only intimidated, neither killed nor took property. After that, the author detailed the punishments in the style of 'al-laf wa al-nashr al-murattab'. 'Na al-qatl jazauhu al-qatl' – when the robber only killed a person, his punishment is only that he be executed. 'Wa al-qatl wa al-akhdh' – the robber killed and also took property, so his punishment is crucifixion. 'Wa akhdh al-mal' – when the robber only took property and did not kill, his punishment is cutting of the hand and foot from opposite sides, i.e., the right hand and left foot. 'Wa al-takhwif' – when the robber only intimidated, neither killed nor took property, his punishment is exile, i.e., perpetual imprisonment. When a group of robbers commit a crime from among these types, all of them will be subjected to the same punishment that corresponds to that crime. It is not meant that each individual is subjected to the punishment for the type of crime he committed. For example, a group committed highway robbery: some killed, some took property, some intimidated; then all of them will be subjected to crucifixion. It is not that the murderer is executed, the property-taker is cut, and the intimidator is imprisoned. This division does not apply; rather, all of them in this case are under crucifixion. Upon that, it is narrated in the hadith that these punishments are explained in this manner. And this narration is from Ibn Abbas, which the author of al-Talwih has mentioned in al-Talwih. So let it be considered. When he takes and kills, according to Abu Hanifa: when the robber both kills and takes property, in this case his punishment was crucifixion. Then Imam Abu Hanifa specified crucifixion for this state alone, meaning that the punishment of crucifixion cannot come in other types except this crime. He did not specify this state of crime exclusively with crucifixion; rather, in this state he allowed four types of punishments, the detail of which is: He may cut then kill – i.e., cut the hand and foot from opposite sides and then kill; or crucify – i.e., after cutting, execute by crucifixion; or he may kill – i.e., only execute; or crucify – i.e., only execute by crucifixion. Because the crime can be considered as one or multiple. That is, in one respect it is cutting off the road (qat' al-marrah), meaning highway robbery has been committed on passersby, so in this respect it is one crime, therefore one punishment – either execution or crucifixion – can suffice. And there is also possibility of multiplicity in this crime, because the robber has done two things: taking property (which is cutting) and killing (which is a cause of execution). So the rulings of both these causes can be applied together. Therefore, cutting and execution or cutting and crucifixion are possible, just as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did with the Urayniyyin: he cut and then placed them in al-Harrah until they died.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Quranic verse on highway robbery (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33). The author first presents an objection: because the verse uses 'aw' (or), it might imply that the ruler has a choice among the four punishments. The response explains that 'aw' here indicates correspondence of each punishment to a specific type of crime, not a general choice. The author then details the four categories of crimes (killing only, killing and taking property, taking property only, intimidation) and their corresponding punishments (execution, crucifixion, cutting of hand and foot from opposite sides, exile/imprisonment). A specific case arises when a group commits different offenses; the ruling is that all are subjected to the most severe punishment (crucifixion), not individual punishments. The author then discusses Abu Hanifa's view on the case where the robber both kills and takes property: although the verse specifies crucifixion for that combination, Abu Hanifa allows all four punishments because the crime can be seen as either a single act (highway robbery) or two separate acts (theft and murder). This is supported by the hadith of the Urayniyyin, where the Prophet combined cutting with execution. The passage guards against a literal reading of 'aw' as pure choice, emphasizing a nuanced understanding based on the crime's nature.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle that can indicate either choice or distribution, here interpreted as distribution (correspondence) by the author.
قاطع الطريق (qati' al-tariq): Highway robber; one who waylays travelers with the intent to steal, kill, or terrorize.
صلب (salab): Crucifixion; a punishment that may include execution on a cross.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation as explained in the passage, the word 'aw' (or) in Quran 5:33 primarily indicates:
A) a free choice for the ruler among the four punishments
B) a correspondence of each punishment to a specific type of crime
C) that the ruler must combine all punishments
D) that only the most severe punishment should be applied

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul approach to 'aw' in legal texts is to examine contextual indications (qara'in) to determine whether it implies choice or distribution; Quran 5:33 is a case where distribution is the correct interpretation.

Linguistic Analysis of Masah: The Rule of 'ب' vs 'على'
Linguistic analysis of 'ب' vs 'على' in masah verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic distinction between 'masaha bi' and 'masaha 'ala' to derive the extent of wiping required in wudu and tayammum.

Core Idea
When 'ب' indicates the instrument, wiping covers the entire locus; 'على' treats the locus like an instrument, implying partial wiping.

This lesson explores a subtle but crucial linguistic principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the difference between the prepositions 'ب' and 'على' when used with the verb 'masaha'. The passage examines how this distinction determines whether wiping must cover the entire organ or only part of it. We will see how the Hanafi school resolves an apparent contradiction when the same preposition 'ب' appears in the tayammum verse but complete coverage is required, using both the principle of substitution (khalaf) and a well-known hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic rule for 'ب' in masah
Note the author's claim: when 'masaha' is used with the preposition 'ب', the 'ب' indicates the instrument (ālah), making the verb transitive to the entire locus. For example, 'masahtu al-ḥā'iṭa bi-yadī' means the wiping covers the whole wall.
The key is that 'ب' here is not a mere preposition but signals the tool, so the locus is fully affected.
2
Contrast with 'على' in masah
When 'masaha' is used with 'على', as in 'وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ' (wipe your heads), the 'على' enters upon the locus. Because 'ب' is originally for the instrument, the locus is likened to an instrument, and only partial wiping is intended.
The head verse uses 'ب' but the head is the locus; Hanafi analysis treats it as 'على' by interpretation, leading to partial wiping.
3
Apply to tayammum: an apparent contradiction
The tayammum verse uses 'بِوُجُوهِكُمْ', which according to the rule would imply partial wiping. Yet complete coverage of the face is obligatory by consensus. The passage presents two answers to resolve this.
This step highlights the tension between a linguistic principle and a established ruling.
4
First answer: substitution (khalaf) argument
Tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, which requires complete washing of the face. Since the substitute inherits the rule of the original, complete wiping is required.
Qiyas: tayammum stands in the place of wudu.
5
Second answer: hadith of Ammar as evidence
The well-known hadith of Ammar (upon striking the ground) explicitly mentions two strikes covering the entire face and forearms. This hadith, though ahad, is accepted because adding to the Quran's apparent meaning is permissible via well-known (mashhūr) hadith.
The hadith overrides the initial linguistic implication, establishing complete coverage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے اتنا مقدار کافی ہو گی جس کے ساتھ مقصود حاصل ہو جائے البتہ اس صورت میں استیعاب محل ضروری ہوگا۔ نحو مسحت الحائط بید کی تو یہاں باید پر داخل ہے جو الہ مسیح ہے يتعدى الى المحل تو فعل مسح بواسطه با کے متعدی الی المحل یعنی ابی الحائط ہو جائیگا فیتنا دل کلہ یعنی مسح کل حائط کو متناول ہو گا لان الحائط اسم للمجموع کیونکہ حائط مجموع دیوار کا نام ہے اور یہ مقصود بالذات ہونیکے طور پر مذکور ہے فیراد کہ تو کل حافظ مراد ہو گی سنخلاف یہ کے کہ اس کے اندر کل مراد نہیں بلکہ صرف اتنا مقداد مراد ہوگی جس کے ساتھ مسح ہو سکے وہ ہے مس بباطن الكف دان دخلت فی المحل اگر لفظ بار محل پر داخل ہو جیسے را مسحوا بو ڈسکم میں کہ راس محل مسح ہے۔ لا یتناول كل المحمل تو یہ مسیح کل محل کو متناول اور شامل بو نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس وقت محل شبیه بالالہ ہو جائیں گے چونکہ یہ حرف بار مخصوص بالالہ ہے اور داخل على المحل ہے تو لا محالہ یہاں محل کو تشبیه بالاتر ہوگی فلا یراد کله توکل محل مراد نہیں بلکہ بعض حصہ محل کا یعنی راس کامراد ہوگا تقديره الصفوها بروسكم اى الصقوا المسح بروسکم تو مراد ہو گا بعض الراس اور اس بعض کو حدیث ناصیہ نے بیان فرما دیا کہ بقدر ناصیہ یعنی ربع رآس کا مسح فرض ہے ۔ وانما يثبت استعیاب الوجه في التیمی المیہ ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ آیتہ تیم میں ہے وامسحوا بوجو محکم اور باداخل علی المحل ہے تو پھر حسب ضابطہ وجہ کا استیعاب بالمسح تیم میں واجب نہ ہو حالانکہ استیعاب وجہ بالاتفاق واجب ہے تو اس کے دو جواب دیتے اول لان المسح خلف عن الغسل یعنی یہ مسح وجہ خلف ہے غسل وجہ کا جو وضو میں ہوتا تھا چونکہ غسل وجہ میں استیعاب واجب ہے اور مسح فی القیم اس کا خلف اور قائمقام ہے اس لئے اس میں بھی استیعاب واجب ہے او بحدیث عمار یہ دوسرا جواب ہے یعنی تسلیم ہے کہ حسب ضابطہ تمیم میں وجہ کا بعض مراد ہوتا لیکن چونکہ حدیث عمار میں مذکور ہے انما یکفیک ضربتان ضربته للوجه وضربته للذراعین تو اس حدیث میں کل وجہ مراد ہے اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے ہزار به على الكتاب اس کے ساتھ کتاب اللہ کے مفہوم پر زیادہ جائز ہے لہذا کتاب کے لحاظ سے بعض وجہ مراد ہو سکتا تھا لیکن حدیث مشہور نے کل وجہ کا مسح واجب قرار دیا اس کے ساتھ کتاب اللہ پر زیادہ صحیح ہے۔
This much amount will be sufficient with which the purpose is achieved, however in this case, complete coverage of the locus is necessary. For example: 'I wiped the wall with my hand' – here 'ب' enters upon the meaning of the instrument of wiping, making the verb transitive to the locus, so the wiping becomes transitive to the locus, meaning the wall, thus it encompasses the entire wall because 'wall' is a name for the totality and it is mentioned as the intended object itself. So the entire wall is intended. Unlike the case where 'على' enters upon the locus, like 'وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ' where the head is the locus of wiping. It does not cover the entire locus because then the locus becomes similar to the instrument. Since 'ب' is specific to the instrument and enters upon the locus, inevitably the locus is likened to the instrument, so the entire locus is not intended, but rather a part of the locus, i.e., some of the head is intended. Its interpretation is: 'attach the wiping to your heads', meaning some of the head. And this part is specified by the hadith of al-Nasiyah as the amount of the forelock, i.e., one quarter of the head is obligatory to wipe. And the completeness of the face is established in Tayammum – this is an answer to an objection. The objection is that in the verse of Tayammum it is 'وَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ' and 'ب' enters upon the locus, so according to the rule, complete coverage of the face by wiping in Tayammum would not be obligatory, whereas complete coverage of the face is obligatory by consensus. They give two answers: first, because the wiping is a substitute for washing – this wiping of the face is a substitute for the washing of the face which was in wudu; since complete coverage is obligatory in washing the face, and this wiping is its substitute and stands in its place, therefore complete coverage is obligatory here. Second, by the hadith of Ammar: it is conceded that according to the rule, part of the face would be intended in Tayammum, but since it is mentioned in the hadith of Ammar 'It suffices you two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the forearms', in this hadith the entire face is intended, and this hadith is well-known. Adding to the meaning of the Book is permissible, so from the perspective of the Book, some of the face could be intended, but the well-known hadith has made wiping the entire face obligatory. Adding to the Book by means of it is correct.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the prepositions 'ب' and 'على' in the context of ritual wiping (masah). The author explains a key Hanafi linguistic principle: when the verb 'masaha' is used with the preposition 'ب' (e.g., 'masahtu bi'l-ha'it'), the 'ب' indicates the instrument, making the verb transitive to the locus, and the entire locus is covered. When used with 'على' (e.g., 'masahtu 'ala ra'si'), the 'على' enters upon the locus, but because 'ب' is originally for the instrument, the locus is treated like an instrument, and only partial wiping is required. This is applied to the Quranic verse of wudu (وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ) where only part of the head is wiped, specified by hadith as one quarter. However, in Tayammum, the verse uses 'بِوُجُوهِكُمْ', which by this rule would indicate partial wiping, but the author gives two reasons for complete coverage: first, Tayammum is a substitute for wudu (which requires complete washing of face), so it inherits the rule of completeness; second, the well-known hadith of Ammar explicitly mentions two strikes covering the whole face and hands. This shows the Hanafi method of resolving apparent conflicts between a linguistic principle and a confirmed hadith.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping; passing a wet hand over a body part for purification.
ب (bā'): Preposition indicating the instrument (alāh) by which the action is performed; makes the verb transitive to the locus and implies complete coverage.
على ('alā): Preposition indicating superiority or attachment; when it enters upon the locus of wiping, it implies partial coverage because the locus is likened to the instrument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in the passage, why is complete wiping of the face obligatory in Tayammum despite the Quranic verse using the preposition 'ب'?
A) Because 'ب' in the Tayammum verse is interpreted as 'على' to indicate completeness.
B) Because Tayammum is a substitute for washing the face in wudu, and the complete coverage obligation is transferred, supported by the hadith of Ammar.
C) Because all verses with 'ب' require complete coverage of the locus.
D) Because the face is a small area and must be covered entirely to ensure purification.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the apparent conflict between linguistic implication and established ruling by using the principle of substitution (khalaf) and supplementary hadith evidence, demonstrating a holistic approach to deriving legal rulings.

The Hanafi Reading of Quran 3:7 and the Knowledge of Mutashabihat
Analyzing the two qira'at of Quran 3:7 and the Hanafi stance on mutashabihat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two qira'at of Quran 3:7, explain the Hanafi preference for waqf on 'illa Allah', and apply the resulting usul principle regarding the knowledge of mutashabihat.

Core Idea
The Hanafi reading stops at 'illa Allah'; only Allah knows ta'wil of mutashabihat, and the raskhun only affirm faith.

This lesson delves into the classical Hanafi analysis of Quran 3:7, focusing on a key qira'a difference that determines the theological stance on ambiguous verses. By understanding the grammatical arguments and the usul principles behind the preferred reading, you will grasp why the Hanafi school firmly holds that even the most knowledgeable scholars do not know the interpretation of mutashabihat, but rather affirm their faith in Allah's wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two qira'at
The passage describes two readings: one with a mandatory waqf (pause) on 'illa Allah', making 'wa al-rasikhun' a new subject, and another without waqf, conjoining 'al-rasikhun' to 'Allah' under the exception.
The first reading is preferred by the Hanafis.
2
Analyze the grammatical argument
The alternative reading requires deleting a mubtada (وهم) before 'yaqulun', which is against the principle of avoiding deletion (al-hazf khilaf al-asl). The Hanafi reading is grammatically simpler.
Deletion is permissible only when necessary; here it is avoidable.
3
Examine the contextual evidence
The Quran itself attributes the pursuit of ta'wil to the deviated (zaygh), while the raskhun are described as saying 'amanna bihi' and praying for guidance. This supports the Hanafi reading.
The deviated seek fitna and ta'wil; the raskhun submit.
4
Derive the usul principle
Based on the Hanafi reading, the principle is that the knowledge of mutashabihat is exclusive to Allah; no human, however learned, can know the intended meaning. This has implications for fiqh and 'aqida.
This conservatism avoids speculative interpretation.
5
Apply to a parallel verse
The principle extends to other mutashabihat verses. For example, the 'yad Allah' verse is to be affirmed without querying how.
The illa is the same: protection from deviation.

ایک ابتلاء جاہل دوسری ابتلاء عالم ان میں سے ابتلا عالم اعظم ترین ہے کیونکہ جو بلوئی اور آزمائش ترک محبوب میں ہوتی ہے اعظم اور اشتق ہوتی ہے بنسبت اس آزمائش کے جو غیر مقصود کے طلب میں ہوتی ہے جاہل میں ثانی قسم کا ابتلا ہے اور راسخ فی العلم میں پہلے قسم کا تو راسخ فی العلم کے لئے ضروری ہو جاتا ہے کہ اس معاملہ میں سب کچھ اللہ تعالیٰ کے حوالے کر دے اور اپنے آپ کو عجز اور بے بسی کے راستہ میں ڈال دے کہ ادراک سے بجز یہ بھی ایک قسم کا ادراک و علم ہے ۔
It is upon that which is the mudaf ilayh of the word hukm and is majrur, so the word mutashabih is majrur by way of atf, and the word 'al-khuruf' is in atf to the word 'al-talab' which is khabr of hukm al-khafi and is marfu', and hukm al-mukhfi is mubtada, and there is one waw and it is mentioned in al-mutashabih. According to the majority, this atf is permissible provided that the majrur comes first; therefore it is said 'al-mabiy dar muqaddam', and that is the word al-mukhfi and its ma'tuf is the word al-mutashabih. For example, 'fi al-dari Zaidun wa hujratu Amrin' is permissible. Similarly, our mentioned atf is also correct, i.e., the ruling of mutashabih is: stop seeking the intended meaning (tawaqquf 'an talab al-murad). All the ma'tufat of hukm al-khafi [which is] al-talab are from this category, upon belief in its truth (i' tiqad al-haqiyyah), i.e., to believe that whatever it may intend is true in the sight of Allah, even if we do not know. According to us, i.e., according to the Hanafis, on the reading of waqf on 'illa Allah', i.e., some scholars make the waqf obligatory on 'illa Allah' in the saying of Allah: 'wa ma ya'lamu ta'wilah illa Allah wa al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm yaqulun', and then the speech from 'wa al-rasikhun' is a new beginning. And some read without waqf, rather they join 'al-rasikhun' to the word 'Allah' and include it under the exception. According to the first reading, i.e., when the waqf is on 'illa Allah', then the raskhun fil ilm do not know the meaning of the mutashabihat, and this is the madhhab of our Hanafi scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). And preferring this reading, he said: 'Wa hadha ayqa bi nazm al-Qur'an'. He presented two reasons for its being more fitting: first, that following the mutashabihat and searching for their meaning is what Allah has made the portion of the deviated ones, as per His saying: 'fa amma alladhina fi qulubihim zayghun fa yattabi'una ma tashabaha minhu ibtigha al-fitnati wa ibtigha ta'wil', and the portion of the firm in knowledge is to affirm its truth and to acknowledge their inability to comprehend the intended meaning. This is understood from Allah's saying: 'yaquluna amanna bihi kullun min 'indi Rabbina', i.e., whether we know or not, we believe in it and affirm that all is from our Lord. This is the work of the firm in knowledge, and they ask: O Lord, protect us from this deviation (la tuzigh qulubana). The second reason for preference: according to the other madhhab (without waqf), the word 'yaquluna amanna' would be the khabar of a deleted mubtada, because when there is no waqf on 'illa Allah' and 'al-rasikhun' is conjoined to 'Allah' under the exception, the estimated phrase is 'wa hum yaquluna amanna bihi'. In our madhhab, we do not have to resort to deletion, rather 'wa al-rasikhun' is mubtada and 'yaquluna amanna bihi' is its khabar, and deletion is contrary to the principle. This is the answer to an objection: if the firm in knowledge have no share in the knowledge of mutashabihat, what is the benefit of their revelation? The answer is that the purpose of revelation is the test of the firm in knowledge. He explains: just as a person who is afflicted with one kind of ignorance is tested by deep travel in seeking knowledge, similarly the firm in knowledge are tested by being told to stop seeking the meaning and to restrain their intellect. For the training of a dullard is done by making him run, while the testing of a noble horse is done by pulling the reins. The test of the firm in knowledge is greater because it involves abandoning what is beloved, which is more severe than seeking something not intended. Therefore, the firm in knowledge must surrender everything to Allah and become annihilated in the ocean of finitude. It has been said: 'the inability to comprehend comprehension is comprehension' ('ajz 'an dark al-idrak idrak), i.e., this is a kind of knowledge.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the verse from Surah Al-Imran (3:7) regarding mutashabihat. The author explains the grammatical construction of the phrase and the two qira'at (readings) concerning the waqf (pause) on 'illa Allah'. According to the Hanafi madhhab, the preferred reading is to stop at 'illa Allah', making the following phrase 'wa al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm yaqulun' a new sentence, meaning that only Allah knows the interpretation, while the firm in knowledge do not know it but affirm their faith. Two reasons are given for this preference: first, the Quran itself attributes the pursuit of interpretation to the deviated, whereas the firm in knowledge only affirm and pray for guidance; second, the alternative reading requires deleting a word (mubtada), which is contrary to the original principle. The passage also answers an objection: if the firm in knowledge do not know the meaning, why were the verses revealed? The answer is that they are a test for the believers, requiring them to submit to Allah's knowledge and acknowledge their own limitation, which is a greater trial than ignorance.

Key Terms
متشابه (mutashabih): Verses of the Quran whose meaning is ambiguous and cannot be definitively understood by humans.
وقف (waqf): Pausing in recitation; a qira'a issue affecting meaning.
راسخون فی العلم (al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm): Those firm in knowledge; for Hanafis, they do not know the ta'wil but affirm faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the meaning of 'wa al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm yaqulun amanna bihi' in the context of mutashabihat?
A) The firm in knowledge know the interpretation of mutashabihat.
B) The firm in knowledge say, 'We believe in it' without knowing the interpretation.
C) The firm in knowledge teach the interpretation to others.
D) The firm in knowledge actively seek the interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's stance on mutashabihat is rooted in a specific qira'a that distinguishes the role of the firm in knowledge as believers, not interpreters.

The Objection Against Linguistic Evidence’s Certainty
Raising an objection that linguistic evidence does not yield certainty and beginning the response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the objection that dalil lafzi does not yield certainty and identify its two conjectural foundations: naql al-lugha and nahw.

Core Idea
Linguistic evidence yields probability, not certainty, because its foundations—language transmission and grammar—are conjectural.

This lesson presents a foundational objection in usul al-fiqh: that linguistic evidence (dalil lafzi) cannot produce certainty (yaqin) because it rests on matters of conjecture (zann). The objection targets the reliability of deducing legal rulings from Arabic words and grammar. Understanding this challenge is critical for grasping the Hanafi position on textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The passage begins by stating that there is an objection and an answer. You must first locate the claim: dalil lafzi does not yield certainty.
The objection is not the final position of the text; it is a challenge to be answered.
2
Define dalil lafzi as per the text
The text defines dalil lafzi as inference from lexical meanings of words according to Arabic grammatical rules. Note that this includes both vocabulary (lugha) and syntax (nahw).
This definition clarifies what is being critiqued.
3
Analyze why it is considered zanni
The objection argues that qiyas (inference) built on zanni foundations cannot yield certainty. It then identifies two existential matters (amr wujudi) that are zanni: naql al-lugha (transmission of language) and nahw (grammar).
The text also mentions non-existential matters (amr 'adami) but cuts off; focus on the existential ones.
4
Connect to broader usul debate
This objection is raised against the reliability of linguistic interpretation. The Hanafi school later responds by distinguishing types of linguistic evidence, some of which can be qat'i through tawatur or clear dalala.
This sets up a key difference between Hanafi and Mutakallimin usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسئلۃ) اس مسئلہ میں ایک اعتراض اور اس کا جواب ہے ۔ خلاصہ اعتراض یہ کہ دلیل لفظی مفید یقین نہیں ہے اور دلیل لفظی سے مراد یہ ہے کہ الفاظ کے مفہومات وضعیہ سے قوانین عربیہ کے تحت جو استدلال کیا جائے گا یہ لفظی ہے اور یہ مفید یقین نہیں ہے ۔ لانه مبنی آلو کیونکہ دلیل لفظی کی مدار امور ظنیہ پر ہے اور جوشی مبنی علی الظن ہو وہ مفید یقین نہیں ہوسکتی امرثانی تو ظاہر ہے البتہ امراول یعنی یہ کہ دلیل لفظی امور ظنیہ پر مبنی ہے اس کو ثابت کیا کہ چند امور وجود یہ پر اور چند امور عدمیہ پر مبنی ہے جو تمام کے تمام فنی ہیں اور امور وجود یہ یہ ہیں نقل لغت کیونکہ معانی وضعیہ مفردات کے لغہ سے معلوم ہوتے ہیں والنحو کیونکہ مینات ترکیبیہ
(Issue) In this issue there is an objection and its answer. Summary of the objection: That dalil lafzi does not yield certainty. By dalil lafzi is meant the inference made from the lexical meanings of words according to the rules of Arabic grammar. This does not yield certainty. Because it is based on conjectural matters. And anything based on conjecture cannot yield certainty. The second point is obvious; however, the first point, that dalil lafzi is based on conjectural matters, needs proof. It is based on several existential matters and several non-existential matters, all of which are conjectural. The existential matters are: transmission of language (naql al-lugha), because the lexical meanings of words are known from language; and grammar (al-nahw), because the structural meanings (al-ma'ani al-tarkibiyyah) ...
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This is a new mas'ala (issue) presented in the text. It begins an objection against the reliability of linguistic evidence (dalil lafzi) in usul al-fiqh. The objection states that dalil lafzi does not produce certainty (yaqin), because it is built on conjectural (zanni) foundations. The author then clarifies that by dalil lafzi he means deducing rulings from the lexical meanings of words under the rules of Arabic grammar. The objection aims to show that such deduction cannot yield certainty because it depends on matters that are only probable: primarily, the transmission of language (naql al-lugha) – i.e., how we know the meanings of words – and the rules of grammar (nahw) that determine the structure. These are not definitive. The text begins to enumerate these existential matters (al-umur al-wujudiyya) but breaks off at the page end. This sets up a classic usul discussion: whether linguistic interpretation can produce certainty or only probability, a key difference between Hanafi and Mutakallimin usul.

Key Terms
دلیل لفظی (dalil lafzi): Inference from lexical and grammatical meanings of words according to Arabic linguistic rules.
ظن (zann): Conjecture or probability; the outcome of dalil lafzi according to the objection.
یقین (yaqin): Certainty; the objection claims dalil lafzi cannot reach it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection presented, why is dalil lafzi not certain (qat'i)?
A) Because it depends on the meanings of words which change over time.
B) Because it is based on conjecture (zann) from sources like language transmission and grammar.
C) Because the Quranic text itself is not preservable.
D) Because it requires ijtihad which is fallible.

Key Takeaway
The objection that linguistic evidence is zanni because it depends on transmitted language and grammar is a central challenge in usul al-fiqh, which the Hanafi school addresses through distinctions in textual categories and transmission types.

The Wisdom of Mutashabihat: A Trial for the Firmly Rooted Scholars
Answering an objection about the benefit of revealing mutashabihat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the purpose of mutashabihat is to test the rasikhun by commanding them to refrain from interpretation, and evaluate the rational argument (dalil aqli) used to support this.

Core Idea
Mutashabihat test the scholars' submission more than the ignorant's striving.

You may wonder: why would Allah reveal verses whose meanings are ambiguous, if even the most learned scholars cannot ascertain them? This passage answers that very question. The wisdom is not to provide hidden knowledge, but to administer a profound trial—one that demands complete surrender. Understanding this shapes the Hanafi approach to Quranic interpretation and humility before the divine text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
State the objection that arises: if mutashabihat verses are not meant to be understood by even the rasikhun, why were they revealed at all?
2
Recognize the Hanafi Answer
The passage directly answers: the very purpose is ibtilah (trial) of the rasikhun. They are tested by being commanded to refrain from seeking interpretation.
This contrasts with the ignorant, who are tested by seeking knowledge.
3
Analyze the Analogy
The author uses an analogy: a lazy person is tested by being made to move and run; a noble horse is tested by pulling the reins and preventing movement. Similarly, the ignorant are tested by exertion in learning, while the scholars are tested by restraint.
This is a rational (aqli) argument—not a scriptural proof, but a logical demonstration of divine wisdom.
4
Understand the Greater Trial
The passage asserts that the test of the scholar is greater because it involves abandoning the beloved (the desire to understand) whereas the ignorant's test is about striving for something not yet attained. The suffering of giving up a cherished pursuit is more severe.
This explains why Allah chose this particular test for the most knowledgeable.
5
Derive the Required Attitude
For the rasikhun, the proper response is absolute surrender (taslim) and recognition of helplessness (ajz). They say 'we believe in it; all is from our Lord.' This is the ultimate station for seekers.
This attitude is the fruit of the trial and the key to deeper faith.
